%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Canonical Locked-Basis Reading of the Longitudinal Actual PDE Coefficient}

\section{1. Direct formula for \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

Let the shell-relevant reduced \(J\)-matrix at the selected intervalley harmonic be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\bigl(\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)\bigr)_{a,b=1}^2,
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:CLK_Uj}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-normal longitudinal singlet coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:CLK_upar_trace}
\end{equation}

In the diagonal Pauli basis \(\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1)\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:CLK_upar_diag}
\end{equation}

So \(u_\parallel\) is literally the shell-normal diagonal asymmetry of the reduced \(J\)-block.

\section{2. Direct formula for \texorpdfstring{$m_\parallel$}{m_parallel}}

In the canonical locked frame,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}.
}
\label{eq:CLK_mcanon}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:CLK_mpar}
\end{equation}

No further reduction is needed.

\section{3. The actual longitudinal scalar}

Hence the unresolved longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:CLK_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{11}
-
(\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0))_{22}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:CLK_Lstar_diag}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Direct longitudinal PDE coefficient}

On the current canonical branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:CLK_lpar}
\end{equation}

Comparing with the reference reduced sheet
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\]
one reads, on this branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\alpha_X L_*.
}
\label{eq:CLK_lc_inference}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual longitudinal reduced coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:CLK_lpar_final}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:CLK_I3}
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:CLK_lpar_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{5. What is now literally left for the longitudinal slot}

The longitudinal slot is therefore no longer structurally open.

The only remaining finite microscopic inputs are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
\qquad
u_\parallel=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:CLK_remaining}
\end{equation}

Once these two numbers are computed from the actual microscopic branch/operator data, the longitudinal actual PDE coefficient is fully populated.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct Reading of the Odd Transverse Coefficient on the Active Route}

The active explicit odd extra-carrier slot is
\[
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
\]

Its induced tangent transport block is
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
\]

Hence the odd projector reads
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
\frac{\mathfrak P_O[V_{EO}]}{\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)}.
}
\]

At one-mediator level,
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\]

In canonical shell normalization \(C_O=1\),
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\]

Therefore the reduced odd transverse coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_c.
}
\]

If one uses the transport-side canonical explicit normalization that absorbs \(J_1\),
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
}
\]

Under the current reference branch choice
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0,
\]
the reference low-order sheet becomes
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2))
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1))
\Bigr]\chi=0
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Finite \(2\times2\) Longitudinal Extraction for the Actual Reduced PDE}

\section{1. Valley-diagonal projected matrices}

Fix the explicit carrier basis
\[
|+,a\rangle:=|G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]

The two valley-diagonal projected blocks at \(p=0\) are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(0)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:FMX_Epm_elements}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, write them in general Hermitian form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:FMX_Epm_matrix}
\end{equation}
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

\section{2. Low eigenvalues and normalized low eigenvectors}

The lower eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2}.
}
\label{eq:FMX_epslow}
\end{equation}

Define the standard ratio parameter
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
}
\label{eq:FMX_rpm}
\end{equation}

Then the normalized low eigenvectors can be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{1+|r_\pm|^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
r_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:FMX_eta}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite \(2\times2\) solution of the valley-side low-mode extraction.

\section{3. Exact closed formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

The intervalley Bloch asymmetry is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-.
}
\label{eq:FMX_Delta00_def}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:FMX_eta}, one gets the exact closed form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:FMX_Delta00}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact longitudinal cancellation condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:FMX_Delta00_zero}
\end{equation}

So the first longitudinal finite audit is reduced completely to the microscopic matrix entries
\[
a_\pm,\qquad b_\pm,\qquad c_\pm.
\]

\section{4. Reduced shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix}

Define the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:FMX_Upar}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal bias is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:FMX_upar}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual unresolved longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:FMX_Lstar}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Finite harmonic formula for \(u_\parallel\)}

In the shell-harmonic basis,
\[
u_a^\pm(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N}c_{a,G}^{(\pm)}e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
\mathsf J_j(x)=\sum_Q\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(Q;0)e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
V_{\mathrm{cell}}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(+)}}\,
\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*+G-G';0)\,
c_{b,G'}^{(-)}.
}
\label{eq:FMX_Uj_finite}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}{2}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Bigl(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Bigr)
\hat n^j\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*+G-G';0).
}
\label{eq:FMX_upar_finite}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel V_{\mathrm{cell}}}{2}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Bigl(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Bigr)
\hat n^j\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*+G-G';0).
}
\label{eq:FMX_Lstar_finite}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Longitudinal coefficient of the actual reduced PDE}

On the current canonical branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:FMX_lambda_par}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:FMX_I3}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:FMX_lambda_par_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Actual reduced PDE coefficient sheet}

The active reference-route reduced PDE coefficient sheet is therefore

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:FMX_lsheet_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:FMX_lsheet_trans}
\end{equation}

Thus the current reference reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:FMX_ref_PDE}
\end{equation}
The first sign is positive because the PDE contains \(-\lambda_\parallel\), while \(\lambda_\parallel\) itself is negative in \eqref{eq:FMX_lambda_par_explicit}.

\section{8. What remains literally to evaluate}

No structural ambiguity remains in the longitudinal slot.

The remaining microscopic inputs are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\pm,\quad b_\pm,\quad c_\pm,\quad u_{11},\quad u_{22},\quad m_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:FMX_remaining}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at the operator level, the true remaining frontier is to evaluate
\[
\boxed{
c_{a,G}^{(\pm)},
\qquad
\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(Q;0),
\qquad
P_0,
\qquad
m^3(P_0)
}
\]
for the final refined locked microscopic operator.

\section{Finite \(2\times2\) Longitudinal Insertion Sheet}

\section{1. Valley-diagonal projected matrices}

Write
\[
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

Their low eigenvalues are
\[
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2}.
\]

Define
\[
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}+\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2}}.
\]

Then the normalized low eigenvectors can be chosen as
\[
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{1+|r_\pm|^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
r_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\section{2. Exact finite formula for \(\Delta_{00}\)}

\[
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
\Sigma_3=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1).
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\]

\section{3. Shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix}

Define
\[
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
\]

Then the longitudinal \(J\)-singlet bias is
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

\section{4. Actual longitudinal coefficient}

On the current canonical branch,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

Using
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\section{5. Current actual reduced PDE coefficient sheet}

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\]

\section{6. Literal remaining microscopic data}

\[
\boxed{
a_\pm,\quad b_\pm,\quad c_\pm,\quad u_{11},\quad u_{22},\quad m_\parallel.
}
\]

Equivalently:
\[
\boxed{
E_\pm(0),\qquad
U_\parallel=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),\qquad
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Finite Insertion Sheet for the Actual Reduced PDE}

\section{1. Valley-side \(2\times 2\) projected blocks}

Write
\[
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,\qquad c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

Their lower eigenvalues are
\[
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2}.
\]

Define
\[
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}},
\qquad
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{1+|r_\pm|^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
r_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the exact intervalley asymmetry is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\]

\section{2. Shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix}

Define
\[
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Equivalently, in the shell-harmonic basis,
\[
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
V_{\mathrm{cell}}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(+)}}\,
\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*+G-G';0)\,
c_{b,G'}^{(-)}.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}{2}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Bigl(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Bigr)
\hat n^j\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*+G-G';0).
}
\]

\section{3. Longitudinal scalar and coefficient}

Let
\[
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Using
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
the actual longitudinal reduced coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\section{4. Transverse coefficients on the active reference route}

The overlap dictionary is
\[
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\]

On the active explicit odd extra-carrier route,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\]

At one-mediator level in canonical explicit normalization,
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
\]

Under the current reference choice
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=\gamma_\perp,
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\]

\section{5. Final current reference reduced PDE}

Therefore the current actual/reference reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

\section{6. Literal remaining microscopic inputs}

So the only remaining microscopic data to insert are
\[
\boxed{
a_\pm,\quad b_\pm,\quad c_\pm,\quad
u_{11},\quad u_{22},\quad
m_\parallel,\quad I_c.
}
\]

Equivalently:
\[
\boxed{
E_\pm(0),\qquad
U_\parallel,\qquad
m^3(P_0),\qquad
I_c.
}
\]

Once these are evaluated from the actual microscopic branch/operator data, the coefficient point
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
is fully populated.

\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_X\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_X\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0
}
\]

\section{Final Full-Microscopic Extraction Route}

\section{1. Shell-projected finite operator}

Choose the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]

Let \(S_*\) be the finite near-resonant harmonic set around \(k_*\), and define the shell projector
\[
\Pi_{S_*}:\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\to \mathcal H_{S_*}(k).
\]

Then the first finite-dimensional operator belonging to the actual full-PDE derivation is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\]

This is the true computational bottleneck. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{2. Low valley projection}

Assume \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\) contains an isolated two-dimensional low-energy sector \(\mathcal V_*\).
Let
\[
\boxed{
P_*:\mathcal H_{S_*}(0)\to \mathcal V_*
}
\]
be the spectral projector onto that valley subspace.

Define the first derivatives
\[
\boxed{
K_i:=\left.\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\]

Then the projected linear valley operator is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{val}}^{(1)}(p)=p_i\,P_*K_iP_*.
}
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{3. Unified coefficient readout}

Inside the valley space, define
\[
\boxed{
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\Tr_{\mathcal H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr),
\qquad
\mu=1,2,3.
}
\]

In the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\),
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\hat n_iM_{3i},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac12\bigl(e_{1i}M_{1i}+e_{2i}M_{2i}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta=\frac12\bigl(e_{2i}M_{1i}-e_{1i}M_{2i}\bigr).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3P_*K_\parallel P_*),
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i.
}
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{4. Minimal axial \(4\times4\) shell ansatz}

On the folded-Bragg \(12\)-mode shell pair, the minimal axial ansatz is
\[
\boxed{
K_i
=
A\,\hat n_i\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_2).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
K_\parallel=A\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K_1=B\,\tau^1\otimes s_1+C\,\tau^1\otimes s_2,
\qquad
K_2=-C\,\tau^1\otimes s_1+B\,\tau^1\otimes s_2.
}
\]

Projecting to the selected positive-valley two-band block,
\[
P_+(\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2)P_+\mapsto \sigma^3,
\qquad
P_+(\tau^1\otimes s_1)P_+\mapsto \sigma^1,
\qquad
P_+(\tau^1\otimes s_2)P_+\mapsto \sigma^2,
\]
so that
\[
\boxed{
h_+(p)
=
A\,p_\parallel\sigma^3
+
B(p_1\sigma^1+p_2\sigma^2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma^1+p_1\sigma^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad \alpha=B,\qquad \beta=C.
}
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{5. What must be computed concretely now}

The folded-Bragg notes localize the remaining finite audit to the primitive-cell Fourier data
\[
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
}
\]

The constant intervalley Bragg block and enriched transverse blocks are controlled by
\[
\boxed{
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha.
}
\]

The local Weyl data are then extracted from
\[
\boxed{
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{act}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
P_*K_iP_*.
}
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\section{6. Honest next step}

So the next nonredundant computation is not another symbolic reduction.

It is exactly this finite operator build:

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)
\;\to\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\to\;
P_*
\;\to\;
K_i
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\to\;
(A,B,C)
}
\]

with
\[
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)=(A,B,C).
}
\]

\section{Explicit \(4\times4\) Folded-Bragg Shell Operator}

\section{1. Shell basis}

Work in the folded-Bragg shell basis
\[
\mathcal H_*=
\mathrm{span}\{\Phi_{+,1},\Phi_{+,2},\Phi_{-,1},\Phi_{-,2}\},
\]
with
\[
\Phi_{+,a}(x)=e^{+iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,
\qquad
\Phi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\]

In this basis, the shell operator is a \(4\times4\) block matrix of the form
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(p) & B^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)\\[1mm]
B^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)^\dagger & E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
where each block is \(2\times2\).

\section{2. First-order expansion near \(p=0\)}

Expand the valley-diagonal blocks as
\[
E_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_2
\pm v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\mathbf 1_2
+
O(|p|^2),
\]
where \(v_\parallel\) is extracted from the \(p_\parallel\)-derivative of the valley-diagonal difference.  
The intervalley block expands as
\[
B^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
M_0+p_1W^1+p_2W^2+O(|p|^2),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
M_0=B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,0),
\qquad
W^i=\partial_{p_i}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\]

Therefore the explicit first-order shell operator is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes M_0
+
p_1\,\tau^1\otimes W^1
+
p_2\,\tau^1\otimes W^2
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]

\section{3. Transverse shell matrices}

The transverse shell matrices are
\[
\boxed{
W^1=\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)\,s^1,
\qquad
W^2=\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)\,s^2.
}
\]

So the first-order operator becomes
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes M_0
+
p_1\,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
p_2\,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)\,\tau^1\otimes s^2
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]

\section{4. Matrix form}

Writing
\[
M_0=
\begin{pmatrix}
m_{11} & m_{12}\\
\overline{m_{12}} & m_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
s^1=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
s^2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i\\
i&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
the shell operator is explicitly
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_*+v_\parallel p_\parallel & 0 & m_{11} & m_{12}+\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1 p_1-i\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2 p_2\\
0 & E_*+v_\parallel p_\parallel & \overline{m_{12}}+\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1 p_1+i\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2 p_2 & m_{22}\\
m_{11} & \overline{m_{12}}+\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1 p_1-i\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2 p_2 & E_*-v_\parallel p_\parallel & 0\\
m_{12}+\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1 p_1+i\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2 p_2 & m_{22} & 0 & E_*-v_\parallel p_\parallel
\end{pmatrix}
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]
Here \(\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^\alpha=\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^\alpha(G_*)\).

\section{5. Principal symbol after the scalar Bragg slot is removed}

On the graded bypass / carrier block, the constant scalar Bragg block is discarded, so the principal first-order shell symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
p_1\,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
p_2\,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)\,\tau^1\otimes s^2.
}
\]

If the transverse amplitudes are equal after calibration,
\[
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)=\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)=:v_\perp,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\perp\bigl(
p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2
\bigr).
}
\]

\section{6. Final projected readout}

Let \(P_*\) be the spectral projector onto the isolated two-dimensional low valley block.
Define
\[
K_i:=\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\big|_{p=0}.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*),
\qquad
K_\parallel=\hat n_iK_i,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2
\Tr(\sigma^aP_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac14\Bigl[
\Tr(\sigma^2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*)
-
\Tr(\sigma^1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*)
\Bigr].
}
\]

Equivalently, in the minimal axial ansatz
\[
A_1(p)
=
A\,p_\parallel\sigma^3
+
B(p_1\sigma^1+p_2\sigma^2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma^1+p_1\sigma^2),
\]
one simply has
\[
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)=(A,B,C).
}
\]

\section{Direct Readout of \(v_\parallel\) and \(\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^{1,2}(G_*)\)}

\subsection{1. Build the complete effective Bloch operator}

Start from the complete microscopic Bloch Hessian
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k),
\]
take the Schur complement against the remote sector, and obtain
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{low,low}}(k)
-
H_{\mathrm{low,rem}}(k)\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,rem}}(k)^{-1}\,
H_{\mathrm{rem,low}}(k).
}
\]

Then project to the folded-Bragg shell subspace \(S_*\):
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\]

\subsection{2. Explicit \(4\times4\) first-order shell form}

In the folded basis
\[
\{\Phi_{+,1},\Phi_{+,2},\Phi_{-,1},\Phi_{-,2}\},
\]
write
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes M_0
+
p_1\,\tau^1\otimes W^1
+
p_2\,\tau^1\otimes W^2
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]

The constant intervalley block is
\[
M_0=B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,0),
\]
and the first transverse derivatives are
\[
\boxed{
W^i
=
\partial_{p_i}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\]

At the shell-fixed current route,
\[
\boxed{
W^1=\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)\,s^1,
\qquad
W^2=\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)\,s^2.
}

So the principal symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
p_1\,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
p_2\,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)\,\tau^1\otimes s^2.
}
\]

\subsection{3. Trace formulas for the three remaining inputs}

Define
\[
K_\parallel:=\partial_{p_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
K_1:=\partial_{p_1}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
K_2:=\partial_{p_2}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\big|_{0}.
\]

Then the raw shell coefficients are read by
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac14\Tr\!\Bigl[(\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2)\,K_\parallel\Bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)
=
\frac14\Tr\!\Bigl[(\tau^1\otimes s^1)\,K_1\Bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)
=
\frac14\Tr\!\Bigl[(\tau^1\otimes s^2)\,K_2\Bigr].
}
\]

Equivalently, before taking derivatives one may read them from the block decomposition:
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac14\Tr\!\Bigl[(\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2)\,
\partial_{p_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\big|_0\Bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*)
=
\frac12\Tr_{2\times2}\!\Bigl[s^1\,\partial_{p_1}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\big|_0\Bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)
=
\frac12\Tr_{2\times2}\!\Bigl[s^2\,\partial_{p_2}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\big|_0\Bigr].
}
\]

\subsection{4. Final reduced coefficients from the projected two-band block}

After projecting to the isolated low valley block \(P_*\),
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\left[
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^1P_*K_1P_*)
+
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^2P_*K_2P_*)
\right],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\left[
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^2P_*K_1P_*)
-
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^1P_*K_2P_*)
\right].
}
\]

In the minimal axial ansatz this reduces simply to
\[
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
=
\bigl(v_\parallel,\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*)\bigr)
}
\]
up to the final calibration/projection normalization of the chosen \(P_*\)-basis.

\subsection{5. What must be computed literally now}

So the literal remaining computation is only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) build }H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k),
\quad
\text{(ii) restrict to }H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p),
\quad
\text{(iii) differentiate at }p=0,
\quad
\text{(iv) evaluate the three traces above.}
}
\]

No further structural reduction is needed.

\section{Immediate full-microscopic route}

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{comp}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)

(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{comp}}
=
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a
+
\gamma_L\mathcal I_L
+
\gamma_E\mathcal I_E
+
\gamma_O\mathcal I_O
+\mathrm{h.c.}
}

After eliminating \(X_i^a\),
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}

On the shell-adapted seed family,
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\nu_\parallel\Gamma c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_I,\qquad
g_O=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_J,
\qquad
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.

Therefore the full microscopic closure is reduced to actual evaluation of
\[
\boxed{
\gamma_L,\ \gamma_E,\ \gamma_O
\quad\text{equivalently}\quad
(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
}

\section{Lowest-Order Complete Microscopic Slot Realization}

\section{1. Three exact lowest-order carrier slots}

On the complete minimal extra mixing sector, the three lowest-order invariant candidates are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
=
X_i^a\,n^i\,
\Tr\!\Big[T^a(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\Big],
}
\label{eq:slotL_LO}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal E^{ia},
}
\label{eq:slotE_LO}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
=
X_i^a\,\mathcal O^{ia}.
}
\label{eq:slotO_LO}
\end{equation}

These generate, respectively,

\[
V_{(L)}^\mu(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
V_{(E)}^\mu(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V_{(O)}^\mu(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Hence the complete lowest-order extra mixing sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{\mathrm{extra,LO}}
=
\gamma_L\,\mathcal I_L^{(2)}
+
\gamma_E\,\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)}
+
\gamma_O\,\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
+\mathrm{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:mixextra_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact heavy-field elimination}

Introduce the total \(X\)-source
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}
=
\alpha_X J_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X K_i^a[P,\psi]
+\gamma_L\,\mathfrak L_i^a
+\gamma_E\,\mathfrak E_i^a
+\gamma_O\,\mathfrak O_i^a,
}
\label{eq:Jtot_complete}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathfrak L_i^a,\qquad
\mathfrak E_i^a,\qquad
\mathfrak O_i^a
\]
are the local operator densities corresponding to
\(
\mathcal I_L^{(2)},\mathcal I_E^{(1,1)},\mathcal I_O^{(1,1)}
\).

Then the \(X\)-dependent piece is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_X^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a
+
X_i^a\,\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:LXtot_complete}
\end{equation}

Integrating out \(X_i^a\) gives exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}\mathcal J_i^{a,\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:LeffX_complete}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Shell-adapted seed family and induced three-direction coefficients}

At the explicit Class II quadratic template level, the reduced \(X\)-sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^a X_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\,\xi^b
+\mathrm{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:LX2_template}
\end{equation}

Integrating out \(X_i^a\) yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\label{eq:deltaN_template}
\end{equation}

Now choose the shell-adapted seed family
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{33}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
}
\label{eq:seed_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{ij}^{31}
=
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{32}
=
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
}
\label{eq:seed_trans}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:Gamma_seed}
\end{equation}

Then the three shell-reduced axial coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\label{eq:deltaABC_seed}
\end{equation}

Using the exact shell/defect dictionary
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_c,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_E,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_O,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:gcego_seed}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Direct reduced-coefficient dictionary}

The exact local defect/projector dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,g_c\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E\,I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O\,I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:reduced_dict_gc}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the carrier notation already fixed in the working notes,
\[
g_c\leftrightarrow \lambda_c,
\qquad
g_E\leftrightarrow \Lambda_E,
\qquad
g_O\leftrightarrow \Lambda_O.
\]

So the complete lowest-order closure condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:nondeg_complete}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nondeg_complete_lambda}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Witness Functionals for the Final Class II Coefficient Readout}

\section{1. Axial tensor family}

In the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), the shell-relevant axial tensor family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
}
\label{eq:WF_axial_family}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact witness functionals}

The exact witness functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_{\parallel}[N]
:=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,N^3_{ij},
}
\label{eq:WF_Wpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_I[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}
+
e_{2j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:WF_WI}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_J[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}
-
e_{2j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:WF_WJ}
\end{equation}

For any tensor in \eqref{eq:WF_axial_family}, these extract exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_{\parallel}[N]=A,
\qquad
W_I[N]=B,
\qquad
W_J[N]=C.
}
\label{eq:WF_exact_extract}
\end{equation}

So the final Class II coefficient problem is reduced to constructing the microscopic tensor \(N_{ij}^a\) and applying these three linear functionals.

\section{3. Minimal Class II seed family}

Take the canonical shell-adapted Class II seed family
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
}
\label{eq:WF_m_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
}
\label{eq:WF_cpar_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}
=
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
}
\label{eq:WF_cIJ_seed}
\end{equation}

Inside the exact concrete quadratic Class II reduction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^aX_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\,\xi^b
+\mathrm{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:WF_LX2}
\end{equation}
and integrating out \(X_i^a\) gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\label{eq:WF_deltaN}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:WF_Gamma}
\end{equation}
Then the induced axial coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\label{eq:WF_deltaABC}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Direct readout of the three seed coefficients}

Applying \eqref{eq:WF_exact_extract} to \(\delta N\), we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_{\parallel}[\delta N]=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:WF_Wpar_deltaN}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_I[\delta N]=-\Gamma c_I,
}
\label{eq:WF_WI_deltaN}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_J[\delta N]=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\label{eq:WF_WJ_deltaN}
\end{equation}

Hence the full microscopic Class II coefficient problem is exactly the finite extraction problem for
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J.
\]

\section{5. Reduced PDE coefficient dictionary}

Using the local defect/projector transport dictionary,
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_c,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_E,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_O,
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:WF_gcgego}
\end{equation}

In the concrete Class II transport normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:WF_lambdas}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:WF_nondeg}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:WF_nondeg_c}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Literal remaining microscopic computation}

Compute the actual microscopic projected tensor
\[
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{mic})}
\]
from the final Bloch harmonic matrices \(H_{\Psi X}(k)\) and \(H_{XX}(k)\), then evaluate
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}],
\qquad
W_I[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}],
\qquad
W_J[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}].
}
\]

This yields
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})},
\qquad
c_I^{(\mathrm{mic})},
\qquad
c_J^{(\mathrm{mic})},
}
\]
and hence
\[
\boxed{
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O,
}
\]
and finally
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact projection formula from \texorpdfstring{$K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}$}{Ki(II)} to \texorpdfstring{$N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{mic})}$}{Nij(mic)}}

\subsection{1. Exact microscopic source}

The exact Schur-complement derivative formula is
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}
\bigl(
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k)
\bigr)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\]

At strict heavy-mass leading order,
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\qquad
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
}
\]

\subsection{2. Shell-enriched tensor definition}

After shell reduction, the induced first-order Class II operator is defined by
\[
\boxed{
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
}
\]

So \(N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{mic})}\) is not a new ansatz.
It is the unique shell-enriched tensor obtained by matching the projected first-order operator generated by \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}\) to the canonical shell-enriched form above. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2} :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsection{3. Exact shell seed decomposition}

The shell witness theorem fixes the only three allowed seed channels:
\[
\boxed{
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
=
c_\parallel\,B_{\parallel\,ij}^a
+
c_I\,B_{I\,ij}^a
+
c_J\,B_{J\,ij}^a,
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
B_{\parallel\,ij}^a=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta^{a3},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
B_{I\,ij}^a=\hat n_i e_{1j}\delta^{a1}+\hat n_i e_{2j}\delta^{a2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
B_{J\,ij}^a=\hat n_i e_{2j}\delta^{a1}-\hat n_i e_{1j}\delta^{a2}.
}
\]

So the whole microscopic Class II coefficient problem is reduced to the three scalars
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel,\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J.
}
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{4. Exact witness functionals}

Define the three witness functionals
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel[N]
:=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,N_{ij}^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
W_I[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^1
+
e_{2j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^2
\Bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
W_J[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^2
-
e_{2j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^1
\Bigr).
}
\]

For any tensor in the seed family,
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel[N]=c_\parallel,
\qquad
W_I[N]=c_I,
\qquad
W_J[N]=c_J.
}
\]

Therefore the exact projection formula is simply
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel=W_\parallel\!\bigl[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}\bigr],\qquad
c_I=W_I\!\bigl[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}\bigr],\qquad
c_J=W_J\!\bigl[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}\bigr].
}
\]

This is the wanted exact projection map from \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}\) to the three microscopic Class II coefficients. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{5. Matching to the reduced transport coefficients}

The reduced shell coefficients are then
\[
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\]

On the shell-level reduced Dirac symbol,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,c_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|\,c_I,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|\,c_J,
}
\]
or equivalently, in the local defect/projector dictionary,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\]

So once \(c_\parallel,c_I,c_J\) are computed from the actual Bloch harmonic matrices, the actual reduced PDE coefficients are fixed. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection{6. Literal remaining computation}

The honest last open step is now exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute } \mathcal J(k),\ \mathcal K(k),\ H_{XX}(k)
\text{ on the final working branch,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{build }K_i^{(\mathrm{II})},
\text{ match it to }N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{mic})},
\text{ and apply }W_\parallel,W_I,W_J.
}
\]

Nothing structural remains beyond this finite coefficient extraction. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\section{Final Summary}

The exact microscopic Class II projection route is

\[
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}
\bigl(
H_{\Psi X}H_{XX}^{-1}H_{X\Psi}
\bigr)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
=
c_\parallel B_{\parallel\,ij}^a
+
c_I B_{I\,ij}^a
+
c_J B_{J\,ij}^a
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
c_\parallel=W_\parallel[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}],
\qquad
c_I=W_I[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}],
\qquad
c_J=W_J[N^{(\mathrm{mic})}]
}
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
=
\bigl(\kappa_*|G_*|\,c_\parallel,\ \kappa_*|G_*|\,c_I,\ \kappa_*|G_*|\,c_J\bigr)
}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_EI_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_OI_\theta.
}
\]

So the remaining microscopic frontier is now exactly the finite extraction of
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel,\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J
}
\]
from the actual Bloch harmonic matrices.

\section{Immediate explicit calculations on the mixed odd-active target branch}

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\alpha^2+\beta^2
=
2\left(\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\right)^2
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{128}\,\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2
}
\]

Hence the \(2\times2\) Dirac/Weyl determinant factor is
\[
\boxed{
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{65536}\,
\alpha_X\beta_X^2\,L_*\,\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\]

In rotated transverse coordinates
\[
q_1=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2},
\]
the transverse velocity is
\[
\boxed{
v_\perp
=
\sqrt2\,|\alpha|
=
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,|\beta_X\theta_0\kappa|.
}
\]

Therefore the branch-level dispersion is
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\left(
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\right)^2
p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{128}\,\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,
(q_1^2+q_2^2).
}
\]

Equivalently, since \(q_1^2+q_2^2=p_1^2+p_2^2\),
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\left(
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\right)^2
p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{128}\,\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,
(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,E_*,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,O_*.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,E_*
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,O_*
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,R_*
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,R_*
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\left(
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\right)^2
p_\parallel^2
+
\left(
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\right)^2
(E_*^2+O_*^2)\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{27\pi^2}{65536}\,\theta_0^6\kappa^6\,(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)})^2\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\,\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,(E_*^2+O_*^2)\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\det M_{\mathrm{Dirac}}
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{65536}\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5\,
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,
(E_*^2+O_*^2).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
E_*^2+O_*^2\neq 0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr)^2
+
\bigl(o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}\bigr)^2
\neq 0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Principal + Residual Transverse Pair: Final Insertion}

\section{1. Principal transverse pair from \(TD+DT\)}

The exact projected mixed block is
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
\]

The invariant transverse projectors are
\[
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
\]

At the current minimal branch-level realization,
\[
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(
A_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
A_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr),
\]
\[
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(
B_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
B_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr).
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}]
=
\frac12(A_E+B_E),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}]
=
\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\]

\section{2. Residual correction vector from \(OD+DO+DD\)}

Define
\[
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm rem}
=
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\rm rem}
=
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
(\Delta e_{\rm rem},\Delta o_{\rm rem}).
}
\]

Hence the full transverse pair is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\frac12(A_E+B_E)+\Delta e_{\rm rem},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\frac12(A_O+B_O)+\Delta o_{\rm rem}.
}
\]

\section{3. Reduced PDE coefficients}

Using
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
the reduced coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac12(A_E+B_E)+\Delta e_{\rm rem}
\right],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_\theta\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac12(A_O+B_O)+\Delta o_{\rm rem}
\right].
}
\]

If we also keep the already-closed longitudinal branch coefficient,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\]
then the full reduced PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left(
\frac12(A_E+B_E)+\Delta e_{\rm rem}
\right)
(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2))
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\qquad\qquad\qquad
+
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left(
\frac12(A_O+B_O)+\Delta o_{\rm rem}
\right)
(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1))
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\]

\section{4. Dispersion relation}

The corresponding dispersion is
\[
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
(\alpha^2+\beta^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{27\pi^2}{65536}\theta_0^6\kappa^6(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)})^2\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2
\Bigr](p_1^2+p_2^2),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2
=
\left(\frac12(A_E+B_E)+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\right)^2
+
\left(\frac12(A_O+B_O)+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\right)^2.
}
\]

\section{5. Determinant / nondegeneracy scalar}

The Dirac nondegeneracy scalar is
\[
\det M_{\rm Dirac}
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
therefore
\[
\boxed{
\det M_{\rm Dirac}
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{65536}
\theta_0^5\kappa^5
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\left[
\left(\frac12(A_E+B_E)+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\right)^2
+
\left(\frac12(A_O+B_O)+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\right)^2
\right].
}
\]

\section{6. Sharp survival conditions}

A sufficient strong componentwise survival condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\rm rem}|<\left|\frac12(A_E+B_E)\right|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\rm rem}|<\left|\frac12(A_O+B_O)\right|.
}
\]

A weaker Euclidean sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
\sqrt{(\Delta e_{\rm rem})^2+(\Delta o_{\rm rem})^2}
<
\frac12\sqrt{(A_E+B_E)^2+(A_O+B_O)^2}.
}
\]

Under either condition,
\[
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\[
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm rem}
=
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\rm rem}
=
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14\,E^\mu{}_a\,
\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_a\,\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{AB,\mu}\bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14\,J^\mu{}_a\,
\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_a\,\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{AB,\mu}\bigr],
\qquad
AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}+\Delta e_{\rm rem},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}+\Delta o_{\rm rem},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}].
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{\rm pr}+\Delta e_{\rm rem}\bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,
\bigl(\Lambda_O^{\rm pr}+\Delta o_{\rm rem}\bigr).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
(\Delta e_{\rm rem},\Delta o_{\rm rem})
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Residual block projector sheet}

For \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\), define
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14\,E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu}^{\rm inv}\bigr),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to0}
\frac14\,J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_{AB,\mu}^{\rm inv}\bigr).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\rm rem}
=
\lim
\frac14\,E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\Bigl[
\Sigma_a\bigl(
\mathcal M_{OD,\mu}^{\rm inv}
+\mathcal M_{DO,\mu}^{\rm inv}
+\mathcal M_{DD,\mu}^{\rm inv}
\bigr)
\Bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\rm rem}
=
\lim
\frac14\,J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\Bigl[
\Sigma_a\bigl(
\mathcal M_{OD,\mu}^{\rm inv}
+\mathcal M_{DO,\mu}^{\rm inv}
+\mathcal M_{DD,\mu}^{\rm inv}
\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\]

\section{Exchange-symmetric reduction}

If the projected background and regulator preserve \(O\leftrightarrow D\) exchange symmetry to leading order, then
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;DO}^{(1)}=e_{0;OD}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_{0;DO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OD}^{(1)}.
}
\]

Therefore the residual correction vector reduces to
\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr).
}
\]

\section{Parity selection rule}

For any \(AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\),
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(-\xi)=+\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(\xi)
\ \Longrightarrow\
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}=o_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0.
}
\]

If instead
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(-\xi)=-\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\rm inv}(\xi),
}
\]
then the block is parity-allowed and must be evaluated explicitly.

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{all even} \Longrightarrow r_{\rm rem}=0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{partial even/odd} \Longrightarrow
r_{\rm rem}
=
\sum_{\substack{AB\in\{OD,DO,DD\}\\ \mathcal M_{AB}\ \text{odd}}}
(e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{all odd} \Longrightarrow
r_{\rm rem}
=
(e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\,
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}).
}
\]

\section{Sharpest honest residual form}

\[
\boxed{
r_{\rm rem}
=
2\bigl(e_{0;OD}^{(1)},o_{0;OD}^{(1)}\bigr)
+
\bigl(e_{0;DD}^{(1)},o_{0;DD}^{(1)}\bigr)
}
\]

\section{One-shot computation sheet for the true corrected Jacobian}

\section{1. Input notation for the 12 residual evaluations}

Let
\[
g_A^{\pm}:=G(\delta_f\pm\varepsilon e_A),\qquad
g_E^{\pm}:=G(\delta_f\pm\varepsilon e_E),\qquad
g_O^{\pm}:=G(\delta_f\pm\varepsilon e_O),
\]
and similarly at half-step,
\[
\tilde g_A^{\pm}:=G\!\left(\delta_f\pm\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_A\right),\qquad
\tilde g_E^{\pm}:=G\!\left(\delta_f\pm\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_E\right),\qquad
\tilde g_O^{\pm}:=G\!\left(\delta_f\pm\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_O\right).
\]

Write the components as
\[
g_Y^\pm=
\begin{pmatrix}

g_{E;Y}^{\pm}\\
g_{O;Y}^{\pm}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\tilde g_Y^\pm=
\begin{pmatrix}
\tilde g_{A;Y}^{\pm}\\
\tilde g_{E;Y}^{\pm}\\
\tilde g_{O;Y}^{\pm}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Y\in\{A,E,O\}.
\]

\section{2. Raw centered-difference Jacobians}

The \(\varepsilon\)-Jacobian is
\[
\boxed{
J_f^{[\varepsilon]}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac{g_{A;A}^+-g_{A;A}^-}{2\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{g_{A;E}^+-g_{A;E}^-}{2\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{g_{A;O}^+-g_{A;O}^-}{2\varepsilon}\\[3mm]
\dfrac{g_{E;A}^+-g_{E;A}^-}{2\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{g_{E;E}^+-g_{E;E}^-}{2\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{g_{E;O}^+-g_{E;O}^-}{2\varepsilon}\\[3mm]
\dfrac{g_{O;A}^+-g_{O;A}^-}{2\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{g_{O;E}^+-g_{O;E}^-}{2\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{g_{O;O}^+-g_{O;O}^-}{2\varepsilon}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

The half-step Jacobian is
\[
\boxed{
J_f^{[\varepsilon/2]}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac{\tilde g_{A;A}^+-\tilde g_{A;A}^-}{\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{\tilde g_{A;E}^+-\tilde g_{A;E}^-}{\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{\tilde g_{A;O}^+-\tilde g_{A;O}^-}{\varepsilon}\\[3mm]
\dfrac{\tilde g_{E;A}^+-\tilde g_{E;A}^-}{\varepsilon} &

\dfrac{\tilde g_{O;A}^+-\tilde g_{O;A}^-}{\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{\tilde g_{O;E}^+-\tilde g_{O;E}^-}{\varepsilon} &
\dfrac{\tilde g_{O;O}^+-\tilde g_{O;O}^-}{\varepsilon}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

\section{3. Richardson-upgraded true Jacobian}

The exact practical extraction object is
\[
\boxed{
J_f:=J_f^{\rm Rich}
=
\frac{4J_f^{[\varepsilon/2]}-J_f^{[\varepsilon]}}{3}.
}
\]

So entrywise,
\[
\boxed{
(J_f)_{XY}
=
\frac{1}{3}
\left[
4\frac{\tilde g_{X;Y}^+-\tilde g_{X;Y}^-}{\varepsilon}
-
\frac{g_{X;Y}^+-g_{X;Y}^-}{2\varepsilon}
\right],
\qquad X,Y\in\{A,E,O\}.
}
\]

\section{4. Subtract the fixed quartic baseline}

Let
\[
J_f^{(4)}
=

0.4137780199567714 & -1.2413340598703142 & 3.603395005929136
\end{pmatrix}.

Hence, for example,

\section{5. Frobenius size and invertibility classifier}

Set
\[
\boxed{

Then the hard perturbative size parameter is

\qquad
\lambda_*\approx 3.52129589.

If one prefers the spectral norm, use

\boxed{
\alpha_f=\frac{\|R_f\|_2}{\lambda_*}.

The file’s exact decision theorem uses \(\widehat\alpha_f\) as the entry-only proxy.

\section{7. Adapted-basis mixing fraction}

Use the branch-adapted orthonormal basis

t=\frac{1}{\sqrt{11}}(1,-3,1)^T,\qquad

\section{8. Exact branch decision rule}

With \(\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2\), the exact next move is:

\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f\ge 1
\Longrightarrow
\text{quartic baseline invertibility control fails;}

\Longrightarrow

\section{PROJECT: TECT --- Master Contents for Continuation (Reference PDE Fixed, Mixed-Branch Matching, and Finite Audit Stage)}

\section{Current Stage}

The current research stage is the following:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the explicit odd extra-carrier route is fixed as the current reference low-order PDE route,}
}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the canonical mixed odd-active branch is the structural target branch,}
}
\end{equation}
and the remaining work is only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{finite coefficient insertion, matching, and two finite microscopic audits.}
}
\end{equation}

The exact current separation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Reference route: explicit odd extra-carrier route (forward-computable now),}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Target route: canonical mixed odd-active branch (structurally closed, two finite audits remain).}
}
\end{equation}

\section{What is Already Fixed}

\subsection{1. Canonical mixed odd-active target branch}

The canonical mixed odd-active target branch is fixed by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2}.
}
\end{equation}

Its exact branch-level coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the target mixed branch is no longer waiting on branch-choice logic.
What remains there is only microscopic coefficient population.

\subsection{2. Current reference branch choice}

The current reference branch is fixed by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

The reduced coefficient dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level in canonical explicit normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore, under the reference choice \(\gamma_E=\gamma_O=\gamma_\perp\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Current reference PDE}

The current reference PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_PDE}
\end{equation}

Introducing rotated transverse coordinates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2},
}
\end{equation}
the same reference PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
\bigl(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:MC_ref_PDE_rot}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{ref}}
=
-\sqrt2\,\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\end{equation}

The corresponding dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{\lambda_c^2 I_3^2}{4}\,p_\parallel^2
+
2\left(\frac{\beta_X\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}\right)^2 I_c^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Reference-route nonzero conditions}

The reference route is nondegenerate as soon as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
I_c\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\gamma_\perp\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Matching conditions to the canonical mixed target}

The reference route matches the canonical mixed odd-active target iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:MC_match_long}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:MC_match_trans}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:MC_match_trans},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\end{equation}
so the transverse reference sheet reproduces the canonical mixed odd-active target exactly.

\section{What Remains Open on the Target Mixed Branch}

The canonical mixed odd-active branch is structurally closed, but its fully populated reduced microscopic coefficient point still awaits exactly two finite microscopic audits.

\subsection{(A) Mixed same-shell support insertion}

The branch-consistent sufficient support condition is
\begin{equation}

|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>

\subsection{(B) Mixed-block transverse cancellation audit}

}
\end{equation}

\section{True \(J_f\) 12-Point Audit at the Corrected Seed}

\section{1. Frozen corrected seed and quartic baseline}

Freeze
\[
\delta_f=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096)^T,
\qquad
e_A=(1,0,0)^T,\quad

Use
\[
\varepsilon=10^{-4},
\qquad
\varepsilon/2=5\times 10^{-5}.

The exact quartic baseline is

J_f^{(4)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
10.095240102467715 & -4.991665531859216 & 0.4137780199567714\\

\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
\lambda_*:=\lambda_{\min}(J_f^{(4)})\approx 3.52129589.

\section{2. The 12 evaluation points}

The six coordinate-basis points at step \(\varepsilon\) are
\[
\delta_f+\varepsilon e_A=(0.0097,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f-\varepsilon e_A=(0.0095,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f+\varepsilon e_E=(0.0096,-0.0287,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f-\varepsilon e_E=(0.0096,-0.0289,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f+\varepsilon e_O=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0097),
\]
\[
\delta_f-\varepsilon e_O=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0095).
\]

The six half-step points are
\[
\delta_f+\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_A=(0.00965,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f-\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_A=(0.00955,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f+\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_E=(0.0096,-0.02875,0.0096),
\]
\[
\delta_f-\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_E=(0.0096,-0.02885,0.0096),

\delta_f+\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_O=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.00965),
\]
\[
\delta_f-\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_O=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.00955).
\]

For each point evaluate
\[
G(\delta)=
\begin{pmatrix}
G_A(\delta)\\
G_E(\delta)\\
G_O(\delta)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\section{3. Raw centered-difference Jacobians}

Define
\[
G_Y^{(+)}:=G(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_Y),
\qquad
G_Y^{(-)}:=G(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_Y),
\qquad
Y\in\{A,E,O\},
\]
and similarly at half-step,
\[
\widetilde G_Y^{(+)}:=G\!\left(\delta_f+\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_Y\right),
\qquad
\widetilde G_Y^{(-)}:=G\!\left(\delta_f-\frac{\varepsilon}{2}e_Y\right).
\]

Then the six-point Jacobian is
\[
\boxed{
(J_f^{[\varepsilon]})_{\cdot Y}
=
\frac{G_Y^{(+)}-G_Y^{(-)}}{2\varepsilon},
\qquad
Y\in\{A,E,O\}.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
J_f^{[\varepsilon]}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac{G_A(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_A)-G_A(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_A)}{2\varepsilon}
&
\dfrac{G_A(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_E)-G_A(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_E)}{2\varepsilon}
&
\dfrac{G_A(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_O)-G_A(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_O)}{2\varepsilon}
\\[3mm]
\dfrac{G_E(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_A)-G_E(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_A)}{2\varepsilon}
&
\dfrac{G_E(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_E)-G_E(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_E)}{2\varepsilon}
&
\dfrac{G_E(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_O)-G_E(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_O)}{2\varepsilon}
\\[3mm]
\dfrac{G_O(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_A)-G_O(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_A)}{2\varepsilon}
&
\dfrac{G_O(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_E)-G_O(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_E)}{2\varepsilon}
&
\dfrac{G_O(\delta_f+\varepsilon e_O)-G_O(\delta_f-\varepsilon e_O)}{2\varepsilon}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

At half-step,
\[
\boxed{
(J_f^{[\varepsilon/2]})_{\cdot Y}
=
\frac{\widetilde G_Y^{(+)}-\widetilde G_Y^{(-)}}{\varepsilon},
\qquad
Y\in\{A,E,O\}.
}
\]

\section{4. Richardson-upgraded Jacobian}

The 12-point improved estimate is
\[
\boxed{
J_f^{\rm Rich}
=
\frac{4J_f^{[\varepsilon/2]}-J_f^{[\varepsilon]}}{3}
=
J_f+O(\varepsilon^4).
}
\]

Set
\[
\boxed{
J_f:=J_f^{\rm Rich}.
}
\]

\section{5. Remainder matrix}

Define the exact local remainder
\[
\boxed{
R_f:=J_f-J_f^{(4)}=(r_{ij})_{i,j=1}^3.
}
\]

Its Frobenius size is
\[
\boxed{
S_f:=\|R_f\|_F^2=\sum_{i,j=1}^3 r_{ij}^2.
}
\]

\section{6. Entry-only classifier}

The no-eigensolver invertibility parameter is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f=\frac{\sqrt{S_f}}{\lambda_*}.
}
\]

The antisymmetric fraction is
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
}{2S_f}.
}
\]

The off-diagonal fraction is
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}^2
=
\frac{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
}{S_f}.
}
\]

\section{7. Adapted-basis mixing fraction}

Use the corrected-branch adapted orthonormal basis
\[
t=\frac{1}{\sqrt{11}}(1,-3,1)^T,\qquad
n_1=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1)^T,\qquad
n_2=\frac{1}{\sqrt{22}}(3,2,3)^T,
\]
and let
\[
B=(t\,|\,n_1\,|\,n_2)\in O(3).
\]

Then
\[
\widetilde R_f:=B^TR_fB=(\tilde r_{ij})_{i,j=1}^3.
\]

Define the tangent-coupling projector
\[
\Pi_{\mathcal T}(\widetilde R_f)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\tilde r_{11} & \tilde r_{12} & \tilde r_{13}\\
\tilde r_{21} & 0 & 0\\
\tilde r_{31} & 0 & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2
=
\frac{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
}{S_f}.
}
\]

\section{8. Exact branch decision rule}

Choose
\[
\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2.
\]

Then the next correct local refinement is determined by:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f\ge 1
\Longrightarrow
\text{quartic Jacobian no longer controls invertibility.}
}
\]

\[

\section{Path A Continuation: Final Executable Sheet for Audit A and Audit B}

\section{Status}

We do \emph{not} reopen branch-choice logic, the reduced coefficient dictionary, or the canonical mixed-sheet derivation.

T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad

\item Audit B: mixed-block transverse cancellation audit.

\section{Audit A: exact assembled seven-constant package}

For the canonical mixed branch,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
\end{equation}

Hence the mixed same-shell block is
\begin{equation}
d_+^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
d_-^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(-p)-a_T\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
m^{(T)}(p)
=
B_{z_0}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p).
\end{equation}

The crucial point is that the remaining seven \(TT\)-constants are not independent unknowns.
They are assembled from the already separated \(EE/OO/EO\) data:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO},
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_\bullet^{TT}
\le
\frac12L_\bullet^{EE}
+
\frac12L_\bullet^{OO}
+
L_\bullet^{EO},
\qquad
\bullet\in\{+,-,0\},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\bullet^{TT}
\le
\frac12C_\bullet^{EE}
+
\frac12C_\bullet^{OO}
+
C_\bullet^{EO},
\qquad
\bullet\in\{+,-,m\}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the derivative budgets
\begin{equation}
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
\end{equation}
Then the mixed-branch drift budgets satisfy
\begin{equation}
A_+^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
A_-^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B^{(T)}\le a_TL_0^{TT}.
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{(T)}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{(T)}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{(T)}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
\end{equation}

Hence the exact branch-consistent same-shell sufficient support condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_T\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\end{equation}
Using \(a_T=2\beta_X^2/M_X^2\), this is equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Audit A compressed lower-bound criterion}

Introduce the directly executable assembled upper bounds
\begin{equation}
\overline L_\bullet^{TT}
:=
\frac12L_\bullet^{EE}
+
\frac12L_\bullet^{OO}
+
L_\bullet^{EO},
\qquad
\bullet\in\{+,-,0\},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\overline C_\bullet^{TT}
:=
\frac12C_\bullet^{EE}
+
\frac12C_\bullet^{OO}
+
C_\bullet^{EO},
\qquad
\bullet\in\{+,-,m\},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\overline{\mathcal S}_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
:=
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{OO}
+
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EO}.
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\overline A_+
=
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_T\overline L_+^{TT},
\qquad
\overline A_-
=
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_T\overline L_-^{TT},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\overline B
=
a_T\overline L_0^{TT},
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\overline\varepsilon_A(\rho)
:=
\Bigl[
(\rho \overline A_+ + \overline C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho \overline A_- + \overline C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho \overline B + \overline C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
\end{equation}

Define the Audit A margin
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_A(\rho)
:=
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
-
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\overline{\mathcal S}_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
-
\overline\varepsilon_A(\rho).
}
\end{equation}

Then a sufficient condition for Audit A to pass is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_A(\rho)>0.
}
\end{equation}

This is the final nonredundant support-side test.

\section{Audit B: exact decomposition into principal pair plus residual tail}

The already explicit \(K\)-sector pair is
\begin{equation}
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 I_{\psi\theta}\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 I_{\psi\theta}\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently, for the tanh defect,
\begin{equation}
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 C_\psi\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 C_\psi\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\end{equation}

Now define the full mixed correction as
\begin{equation}
\Delta e_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}},
\end{equation}
with principal pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)},
}
\end{equation}
and residual tail
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}}
:=
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}
:=
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}.
\end{equation}

Therefore the final reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}}
\Bigr),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Bigl(
o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}
\Bigr).
\end{equation}

\section{Audit B sharp sufficient survival tests}

A strong sufficient survival condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}|+|\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}}|
<
|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}|+|\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}|
<
|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|.
}
\end{equation}
Indeed, by the triangle inequality,
\begin{equation}
|\Lambda_E|
\ge
|e_{0;K}^{(1)}|-|\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}|-|\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}}|,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
|\Lambda_O|
\ge
|o_{0;K}^{(1)}|-|\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}|-|\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}|.
\end{equation}
Thus the above inequalities imply
\[
\Lambda_E\neq 0,
\qquad
\Lambda_O\neq 0.
\]

A weaker but still sufficient sign-coherent version is the following:
if
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{sgn}(\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}})=\operatorname{sgn}(e_{0;K}^{(1)}),
\qquad
\operatorname{sgn}(\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}})=\operatorname{sgn}(o_{0;K}^{(1)}),
\end{equation}
then only the residual tail must be controlled by
\begin{equation}
|\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}}|
<
|e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}|,
\qquad
|\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}|
<
|o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}|.
\end{equation}

\section{Audit B exact execution order}

The nonredundant order is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item extract the invariant projected kernel
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT})\Pi_Q;
\]
\item compute
\[
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}],
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}];
\]
\item only after that, add the tail from \(OD+DO+DD\).
\end{enumerate}

This order is forced because \(TD+DT\) is the principal transverse mixed source, while \(DD\) is structurally more likely to renormalize an existing transverse carrier than to create it from nothing.

\section{What is actually closed now}

At this point, the exact new closure is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Audit A is reduced to one assembled scalar margin \(\mathfrak G_A(\rho)\);
\item Audit B is reduced to one principal-pair extraction \((\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}},\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}})\) plus one residual-tail bound;
\item no independent new symbolic reduction is needed.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the true next microscopic computation is no longer ``derive another theorem'' but simply:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }(e_{0;TD}^{(1)},o_{0;TD}^{(1)},e_{0;DT}^{(1)},o_{0;DT}^{(1)})
\text{ first.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The mixed odd-active branch is structurally closed.

Audit A is now a finite insertion inequality:
\[
\mathfrak G_A(\rho)>0.
\]

Audit B is now a finite cancellation audit around the already explicit \(K\)-sector pair:
\[
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}.
\]

Thus the mainline is fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{first }TD+DT,\quad
\text{then }OD+DO+DD,\quad
\text{without reopening any earlier symbolic layer.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The current reference route remains fixed, and the canonical mixed odd-active branch remains structurally closed.

The new nonredundant closure is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Audit A reduces to one assembled scalar support margin } \mathfrak G_A(\rho).
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Audit B reduces to a principal transverse pair from }TD+DT
\text{ plus a residual tail from }OD+DO+DD.
}
\end{equation}

Explicitly,
\[
\mathfrak G_A(\rho)
=
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
-
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\overline{\mathcal S}_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
-
\overline\varepsilon_A(\rho),
\]
and Audit A passes if
\[
\mathfrak G_A(\rho)>0.
\]

Also,
\[
\Lambda_E=e_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_{0;K}^{(1)}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}+\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}},
\]
with
\[
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}=e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}=o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}.
\]

Therefore the exact next mainline computation is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the principal }TD+DT\text{ transverse pair first,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{and only then add the }OD+DO+DD\text{ tail correction.}
}
\]

No earlier symbolic reduction should be reopened.
