\section{Audit B Principal Pair from the \(TD+DT\) Block}

\section{Goal}

On the current mixed-branch PDE path, the principal transverse correction is carried by
the mixed \(TD+DT\) block.
The task is to identify the leading pair
\[
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}},
\]
and connect it directly to the reduced PDE coefficients \((\alpha,\beta)\).

\section{1. Projected mixed transverse carrier}

Define the projected mixed first-order kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\end{equation}

The canonical invariant projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal transverse coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\end{equation}

In the present Audit-B notation we simply set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}:=\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}:=\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Generic invariant form of the \(TD\) and \(DT\) blocks}

At the current explicit branch-level realization, the two mixed blocks have the generic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;TD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;TD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;TD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{DT,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DT}(\theta)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
a_{E;DT}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
a_{O;DT}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\end{equation}

Because \(TD\) and \(DT\) mix one shell-gradient/current side with one defect/tangent side,
they are the natural carrier of the linear transverse monomials
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
\]

Thus, at leading order, we may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(
A_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
A_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(
B_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
B_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
(A_E+B_E)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
(A_O+B_O)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{corr}},
}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{corr}}\) starts at higher order and/or receives residual contributions from
\[
OD,\quad DO,\quad DD.
\]

\section{3. Explicit extraction of the principal pair}

Applying the invariant projectors and using the canonical projector normalization already built into
\(\mathfrak P_E,\mathfrak P_O\), one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}=\frac12 A_E,
\qquad
e_{0;DT}^{(1)}=\frac12 B_E,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}=\frac12 A_O,
\qquad
o_{0;DT}^{(1)}=\frac12 B_O.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal correction pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)}
=
\frac12(A_E+B_E),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}
=
\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{pr}}=\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Connection to the reduced PDE coefficients}

The exact reduced coefficient dictionary on the current branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

Keeping only the principal \(TD+DT\) part gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
I_\theta\,\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
I_\theta\,\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

So the principal transverse PDE point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}},\beta_{\mathrm{pr}})
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa
\bigl(
A_E+B_E,\,
A_O+B_O
\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Full Audit-B split}

After this principal extraction, the full mixed transverse point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
+
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
+
\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
=
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
+
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
+
\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}},
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{tail}}
=
e_{0;OD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DO}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{tail}}
=
o_{0;OD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DO}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the sharp execution order is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD+DT \ \text{first},
\qquad
OD+DO+DD \ \text{second}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Honest status}

At the current explicit Class-II working level, the relation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}=\frac12(A_O+B_O)
}
\end{equation}
is a correct branch-level reduced summary.

However, it should still be stated honestly that this is not yet the unconditional final microscopic closure of the complete TECT PDE.
The remaining frontier is the literal blockwise differentiation of the full one-defect Hessian and the explicit evaluation of
\[
A_E,\quad B_E,\quad A_O,\quad B_O
\]
on the intended branch.

\section{Conclusion}

The principal transverse audit is now closed algebraically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal reduced PDE coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

So the next nonredundant microscopic task is no longer structural.
It is the explicit Hessian differentiation and projection that determines
\[
A_E,\quad B_E,\quad A_O,\quad B_O.
\]

\section{Source-Level Elimination of \texorpdfstring{$A_E,B_E,A_O,B_O$}{AE,BE,AO,BO}}

\section{Goal}

The previous branch-level transverse summary
\[
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O)
\]
is algebraically correct, but it is not yet the sharpest source-level form.

The next nonredundant step is to eliminate the bookkeeping constants
\[
A_E,\ B_E,\ A_O,\ B_O
\]
and rewrite the principal transverse pair directly in terms of the microscopic
\(JK+KJ\) source on the frozen corrected branch.

\section{1. Exact source split}

After integrating out the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\), the exact quadratic Schur correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta J\delta J^\dagger
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger\bigr)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta K\delta K^\dagger.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the microscopic source sectors are
\[
JJ,\qquad JK+KJ,\qquad KK.
\]

The source/block routing is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ \leftrightarrow OO\text{-longitudinal audit},
\qquad
JK+KJ \leftrightarrow TD+DT\text{-transverse audit},
\qquad
KK \leftrightarrow \text{transverse residual sector}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Principal transverse pair from the \(JK+KJ\) source}

On the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the mixed \(JK+KJ\) source yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
c_O
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:source_cEco}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the principal source-level pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{JK}
=
(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{JK}
=
(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:source_LambdaJK}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal correction pair in the Audit-B notation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:source_Delta_pr}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Elimination of the bookkeeping constants}

Since
\[
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
\]
comparison with \eqref{eq:source_Delta_pr} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12(A_E+B_E)
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12(A_O+B_O)
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_E+B_E
=
2\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_O+B_O
=
2\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

So the \(A/B\)-notation can be eliminated completely in favor of the source-level \(JK\) contraction.

\section{4. Principal-plus-residual reduced PDE coefficients}

The exact reduced coefficient dictionary is
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Separating the principal \(JK\) part and the residual \(KK\) part, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
}
\label{eq:alpha_JK_KK}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
}
\label{eq:beta_JK_KK}
\end{equation}

Thus the transverse audit is now an explicit competition:
\[
\text{principal }JK
\quad\text{vs.}\quad
\text{residual }KK.
\]

\section{5. Sharp dominance criterion}

A sufficient condition that the \(KK\)-residual does not kill the principal pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_E^{KK}|
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|\,|\Lambda_E^{(0)}|,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|\,|\Lambda_O^{KK}|
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|\,|\Lambda_O^{(0)}|.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\beta_X|
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{KK})^2+(\Lambda_O^{KK})^2}
<
|\alpha_X|\,|j\!\cdot\!k|
\sqrt{(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2+(\Lambda_O^{(0)})^2}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Honest odd-channel bottleneck}

At the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation, the corrected notes show that orbit-amplitude corrections alone do not activate the odd transverse witness:
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

Therefore, if
\[
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
\]
then the principal \(JK\)-pair does not by itself open the odd channel.
In that case the first activation of \(\beta\) must come from a genuinely microscopic sign-sensitive insertion and/or the residual completion sector.

This is the sharp current bottleneck for the odd transverse coefficient.

\section{Conclusion}

The principal transverse audit is now closed at the source level.

The bookkeeping constants \(A_E,B_E,A_O,B_O\) are no longer fundamental.
They combine into the explicit \(JK\)-driven pair
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta e_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta o_{\mathrm{pr}}
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK}
\right],
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}
\right].
}
\end{equation}

So the next nonredundant microscopic problem is reduced to the literal evaluation of the three finite quantities
\[
j\!\cdot\!k,
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\]
followed by the residual \(KK\)-dominance check.

\section{Honest Odd-Channel Closure on the Current Working Branch}

\section{Status}

The odd transverse slot is not proven to vanish universally.

What is actually established is the sharper statement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\neq 0
\ \text{is not automatic, and it requires genuinely derivative-resolved and/or phase-resolved microscopic structure.}
}
\end{equation}

Thus the correct logical status is:

\begin{itemize}
\item not ``the odd channel is impossible'';
\item but rather ``the odd channel is not activated by the minimal rigid first-shell orbit-amplitude mechanism alone''.
\end{itemize}

\section{1. No linear odd activation on the frozen corrected seed}

On the sign-resolved first-shell lift of the frozen corrected seed,
\begin{equation}
r^{(ct_1)}_{\rm sub}\cdot\delta_{\rm sub}^{\rm corr}=0,
\qquad
r^{(ct_2)}_{\rm sub}\cdot\delta_{\rm sub}^{\rm corr}=0.
\end{equation}

Therefore the sign-sensitive first-shell transverse factor has no linear corrected shift.
Equivalently, the odd transverse coefficient does not turn on linearly on the present orbit-symmetric corrected branch.

\section{2. Minimal first-shell truncation is insufficient}

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta_{\rm corr})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\rm corr}=0.
}
\end{equation}

Hence orbit-amplitude corrections alone do not generate the odd transverse witness.

This closes the negative result at the current quartic orbit-amplitude level:
the odd slot does not activate there.

\section{3. First genuinely active odd source}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_2(\delta)
=
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}(\delta)
\right]
}
\end{equation}
be the odd transverse source extracted from the mixed \(TD+DT\) block.

Then the corrected odd transverse Hessian response is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
:=
\partial_{\delta_r}\partial_{\delta_s}X_2(\delta)\big|_{\delta=0}.
}
\end{equation}

On the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the leading realization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\text{subleading completion terms}.
}
\label{eq:odd_first_active_slot}
\end{equation}

This is the decisive point:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the first active odd transverse source is the quadratic Hessian response of the mixed }JK+KJ\text{ channel.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Leading corrected odd coefficient}

Since the base odd slot vanishes on the current orbit-symmetric corrected branch and the linear term also vanishes, the leading corrected odd coefficient is inferred to start at quadratic order:
\begin{equation}
X_2(\delta)
=
\frac12 H^{(2)}_{rs}\,\delta_r\delta_s
+
O(\delta^3)
\qquad
\text{(current branch-level inference)}.
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\rm corr}
=
I_\theta\,\frac12 H^{(2)}_{rs}\,\delta_r\delta_s
+
O(\delta^3),
}
\end{equation}
provided the quadratic Hessian slot \eqref{eq:odd_first_active_slot} is nonzero.

\section{5. Honest fallback if the quadratic \(JK+KJ\) slot still vanishes}

If the quadratic mixed \(JK+KJ\) Hessian response vanishes in the intended truncation, then the next odd source must come from the subleading completion terms already isolated in the notes, namely genuinely microscopic derivative-/phase-resolved completion beyond the rigid first-shell orbit-amplitude ansatz.

So the honest branch logic is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{first try }TD+DT\text{ quadratic Hessian response;}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{if that still vanishes, the odd slot moves to subleading completion structure.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The current bottleneck is now sharply fixed.

The odd channel is not activated by:
\[
\text{linear first-shell sign response},
\qquad
\text{or minimal rigid orbit-amplitude corrections alone.}
\]

The first genuinely active odd source on the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{\delta_r}\partial_{\delta_s}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}(\delta)
\right]_{\delta=0},
}
\end{equation}
namely the quadratic Hessian response of the mixed \(JK+KJ\) channel.

Therefore the next nonredundant microscopic task is not another orbit-level closure,
but the explicit evaluation of the finite Hessian matrix
\[
H^{(2)}_{rs}.
\]

\section{Exact Quadratic Hessian Extraction for the Odd Transverse Slot}

\section{Goal}

We now stop speaking schematically and write the odd transverse Hessian response
in the exact operator form that is actually needed for the current branch.

To avoid index collision, let
\[
R,S\in\{A,E,O\}
\]
denote the orbit-amplitude coordinates,
while \(r,u,v,\dots\) are reserved for internal/tangent component indices.

\section{1. Exact starting point}

The exact odd transverse source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_2(\delta)
=
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M^{\mathrm{inv}}_{TD+DT}(\delta)
\right].
}
\end{equation}

Its Hessian coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{RS}
:=
\partial_{\delta_R}\partial_{\delta_S}X_2(\delta)\big|_{\delta=0}.
}
\end{equation}

On the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{RS}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{RS}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\text{subleading completion terms}.
}
\label{eq:H2_master}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact 8-term expansion}

Introduce the shorthand
\begin{equation}
J_0:=\delta J|_{\delta=0},
\qquad
K_0:=\delta K|_{\delta=0},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
J_R:=\partial_{\delta_R}\delta J|_0,
\qquad
K_R:=\partial_{\delta_R}\delta K|_0,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
J_{RS}:=\partial_{\delta_R}\partial_{\delta_S}\delta J|_0,
\qquad
K_{RS}:=\partial_{\delta_R}\partial_{\delta_S}\delta K|_0.
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{align}
\partial_{RS}\bigl(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger\bigr)\Big|_0
&=
J_{RS}K_0^\dagger
+
J_RK_S^\dagger
+
J_SK_R^\dagger
+
J_0K_{RS}^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
K_{RS}J_0^\dagger
+
K_RJ_S^\dagger
+
K_SJ_R^\dagger
+
K_0J_{RS}^\dagger .
\label{eq:H2_8term}
\end{align}

Therefore the exact operator formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{RS}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
J_{RS}K_0^\dagger
+
J_RK_S^\dagger
+
J_SK_R^\dagger
+
J_0K_{RS}^\dagger
+
K_{RS}J_0^\dagger
+
K_RJ_S^\dagger
+
K_SJ_R^\dagger
+
K_0J_{RS}^\dagger
\Big]
+\cdots .
}
\label{eq:H2_exact8}
\end{equation}

This is the exact formula that was still implicit before.

\section{3. Natural linear-current reduction}

Now make the \emph{natural linear-current approximation} around the base branch:
\begin{equation}
\delta J(\delta)=\sum_{R}\delta_R\,J_R+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta K(\delta)=\sum_{R}\delta_R\,K_R+O(\delta^2).
\label{eq:linear_current_ansatz}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
J_0=K_0=0,
\qquad
J_{RS}=K_{RS}=0
\]
at the strict leading linear-current level, so \eqref{eq:H2_exact8} collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{RS}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
J_RK_S^\dagger
+
J_SK_R^\dagger
+
K_RJ_S^\dagger
+
K_SJ_R^\dagger
\Big]
+\cdots .
}
\label{eq:H2_linear_reduced}
\end{equation}

Thus the odd-channel frontier is reduced from a full nonlinear second-derivative problem
to a finite symmetric \(3\times3\) bilinear matrix built from the six pairs
\[
(A,A),\ (E,E),\ (O,O),\ (A,E),\ (A,O),\ (E,O).
\]

\section{4. Load-bearing local kernels}

The notes already fix the load-bearing linearized kernels as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\delta J_R)_i^{\,a}
=
m^a(P_0)\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
\mathcal U_{jR}{}^{b}\,
(-i\partial_j)s_b,
}
\label{eq:J_R_load}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\delta K_R)_i^{\,a}
=
(\partial_i\xi^a)\,
\mathcal V_{jR}{}^{b}\,
(-i\partial_j)s_b.
}
\label{eq:K_R_load}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:J_R_load} and \eqref{eq:K_R_load} into \eqref{eq:H2_linear_reduced},
one sees that every Hessian entry is a projected mixed bilinear of the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{RS}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal C_{RS}
+\cdots ,
}
\label{eq:H2_CRS}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{align}
\mathcal C_{RS}
:=
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
&
J_RK_S^\dagger
+
J_SK_R^\dagger
+
K_RJ_S^\dagger
+
K_SJ_R^\dagger
\Big].
\label{eq:CRS_def}
\end{align}

Equivalently, using
\[
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_c\,
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_c\,\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\]
we may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{RS}
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_c\,
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\Big[
\Sigma_c\,
\Pi_Q
\bigl(
J_RK_S^\dagger
+
J_SK_R^\dagger
+
K_RJ_S^\dagger
+
K_SJ_R^\dagger
\bigr)_\mu
\Pi_Q
\Big].
}
\label{eq:CRS_trace}
\end{equation}

This is the finite projected tensor that must be computed on the frozen corrected branch.

\section{5. Symmetry and the six independent coefficients}

Because \(H^{(2)}_{RS}\) is a Hessian,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{RS}=H^{(2)}_{SR}.
}
\end{equation}
Hence only the six entries
\[
H^{(2)}_{AA},\ 
H^{(2)}_{EE},\ 
H^{(2)}_{OO},\ 
H^{(2)}_{AE},\ 
H^{(2)}_{AO},\ 
H^{(2)}_{EO}
\]
are independent.

So the odd-channel activation problem is now a literal six-number finite audit.

\section{6. Explicit corrected-seed quadratic form}

The corrected frozen branch is
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}=(a,e,o)=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096).
\]

The quadratic odd source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta)
=
\frac12\sum_{R,S\in\{A,E,O\}}H^{(2)}_{RS}\,\delta_R\delta_S.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore, at the corrected seed,
\begin{align}
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
&=
\frac12\Bigl[
a^2 H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
e^2 H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
o^2 H^{(2)}_{OO}
+
2ae\,H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
2ao\,H^{(2)}_{AO}
+
2eo\,H^{(2)}_{EO}
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&=
4.608\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{OO}
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-2.7648\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\label{eq:Q2_explicit_weights}
\end{align}

Thus the odd coefficient becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:beta_corr_Q2}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Sharp practical meaning}

Equation \eqref{eq:Q2_explicit_weights} shows immediately that the most heavily weighted entries are
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE},
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{AE},
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{EO},
\]
while \(H^{(2)}_{AA}\) and \(H^{(2)}_{OO}\) are relatively weakly weighted.

So the odd-channel sign decision on the corrected seed is dominated by a competition between:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
+\ 4.1472\times10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EE}
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\ 2.7648\times10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{AE}
-\ 2.7648\times10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EO},
}
\end{equation}
with a smaller correction from
\[
+\ 9.216\times10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AO}.
\]

\section{Conclusion}

The odd transverse frontier is now reduced to a strict finite problem.

What remains is not a new theorem and not a new branch choice.

It is exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the six projected mixed bilinears }
\mathcal C_{AA},\mathcal C_{EE},\mathcal C_{OO},
\mathcal C_{AE},\mathcal C_{AO},\mathcal C_{EO},
}
\end{equation}
then use
\[
H^{(2)}_{RS}=-(\alpha_X\beta_X/M_X^2)\mathcal C_{RS}+\cdots
\]
inside
\eqref{eq:Q2_explicit_weights}
to decide the sign and nonvanishing of \(\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\).

\section{Final Summary}

The current odd-channel frontier is now reduced to a strict finite audit.

The exact first active odd source is
\[
H^{(2)}_{RS}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{RS}(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\cdots ,
\]
and its exact operator expansion is the 8-term formula.

Under the natural linear-current approximation around the base branch, this reduces to
\[
H^{(2)}_{RS}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
J_RK_S^\dagger+J_SK_R^\dagger+K_RJ_S^\dagger+K_SJ_R^\dagger
\Big]
+\cdots .
\]

Hence only six independent coefficients remain:
\[
H^{(2)}_{AA},\ 
H^{(2)}_{EE},\ 
H^{(2)}_{OO},\ 
H^{(2)}_{AE},\ 
H^{(2)}_{AO},\ 
H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]

At the corrected seed
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
the odd quadratic source is exactly
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]

Therefore the next nonredundant microscopic task is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the six projected mixed bilinears } \mathcal C_{RS},
\text{ hence }H^{(2)}_{RS},
\text{ and decide whether }Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Structural Zero/Nonzero Classification of the Odd Hessian Rows}

\section{Goal}

We now classify the six symmetric odd-Hessian rows
\[
H^{(2)}_{AA},\quad
H^{(2)}_{EE},\quad
H^{(2)}_{OO},\quad
H^{(2)}_{AE},\quad
H^{(2)}_{AO},\quad
H^{(2)}_{EO}
\]
into:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{structural zeros in the rigid truncation}
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the first surviving non-rigid microscopic slots.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Fast practical formulas}

Under the fast working approximation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_rK_s^\dagger+J_sK_r^\dagger+K_rJ_s^\dagger+K_sJ_r^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:odd_fast_master_final}
\end{equation}

Hence explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big],
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_AK_E^\dagger+J_EK_A^\dagger+K_AJ_E^\dagger+K_EJ_A^\dagger
\big],
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_O^\dagger+J_OK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_O^\dagger+K_OJ_E^\dagger
\big],
}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_AK_A^\dagger+K_AJ_A^\dagger
\big],
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_OK_O^\dagger+K_OJ_O^\dagger
\big],
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_AK_O^\dagger+J_OK_A^\dagger+K_AJ_O^\dagger+K_OJ_A^\dagger
\big].
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Rigid-truncation no-go}

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_A=K_E=K_O=0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore every fast row vanishes identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
0.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the rigid first-shell orbit-amplitude ansatz cannot activate the odd witness at all.

\section{3. First surviving non-rigid slot}

Once the rigid truncation is lifted, the corrected-seed contraction weights satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|EE|:|AE|:|EO|:|AO|:|AA|:|OO|=9:6:6:2:1:1.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the first decisive row is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}.
}
\end{equation}

The second-priority rows are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{AE},
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{EO}.
}
\end{equation}

The remaining rows
\[
H^{(2)}_{AO},\quad H^{(2)}_{AA},\quad H^{(2)}_{OO}
\]
are subleading in the corrected-seed contraction.

Thus the first non-rigid microscopic priority order is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(J_E,K_E)\ \text{first},
\qquad
(J_A,K_E)\ \text{and}\ (J_E,K_O)\ \text{second}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Why the \(E\)-sector must be the first test}

At the corrected residual level, a coarse \(A/E\)-symmetric completion is impossible:
it would force
\[
a^2=e^2,
\]
but the corrected seed satisfies
\[
e^2=9a^2.
\]

Therefore the missing microscopic completion must already contain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{non-diagonal }A/E\text{-breaking mixing.}
}
\end{equation}

This is consistent with the Hessian-weight hierarchy above:
the dominant odd-slot sensitivity sits precisely in the \(E\)-sector and in \(A/E\)-mixed rows.

\section{5. Practical sufficient criterion}

A convenient sufficient criterion for odd-slot activation is the \(EE\)-dominance inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|H^{(2)}_{EE}|
>
\frac19\bigl(|H^{(2)}_{AA}|+|H^{(2)}_{OO}|\bigr)
+\frac23\bigl(|H^{(2)}_{AE}|+|H^{(2)}_{EO}|\bigr)
+\frac29|H^{(2)}_{AO}|.
}
\end{equation}

If, in addition, the sign of the \(EE\)-term is constructive in the corrected contraction,
then
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})\neq 0
\]
and therefore
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\neq 0.
\]

\section{6. Honest final classification}

The six rows now split sharply into two categories.

\paragraph{Category I: structural zeros inside the rigid first-shell truncation.}
All six rows vanish identically because \(K_A=K_E=K_O=0\).

\paragraph{Category II: first survivors once non-rigid microscopic structure is allowed.}
The first actual nonzero test is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE},
\]
followed by
\[
H^{(2)}_{AE},\qquad H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]

So the odd-channel frontier is no longer vague.
It is reduced to the explicit non-rigid \(E\)-sector current pair computation.

\section{Conclusion}

The rigid first-shell route is dead for the odd channel:
\[
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0
\quad\text{identically there.}
}
\]

The first meaningful microscopic test beyond that truncation is
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big].
}
\]

Hence the next nonredundant computation is to extract the non-rigid \(E\)-sector pair
\[
(J_E,K_E),
\]
and only then move to the mixed rows
\[
H^{(2)}_{AE},\qquad H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Reduction of the First Non-Rigid Odd Test to Four Background Tensor Inputs}

\section{Goal}

We now reduce the first non-rigid odd test
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE}
\]
to the explicit background tensors that still remain unevaluated on the frozen corrected branch.

The correct point is that the naive undifferentiated local \(JK\) bilinear vanishes, so the first meaningful odd source must be derivative-resolved at the shell point \(G_*\).

\section{1. Exact starting point}

The first active odd transverse Hessian response is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\bigl[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\bigr]
+\cdots ,
}
\label{eq:H2EE_start}
\end{equation}
where the ellipsis denotes subleading completion terms beyond the current fast reduction.

However, the honest microscopic frontier is not the undifferentiated local product itself, because
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2
\]
would imply
\[
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=0
\]
by Pauli anticommutation.

Therefore the true object is the shell-derivative audit
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:H2EE_true_object}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact derivative-resolved \(JK\) block}

The exact mixed derivative block is
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\Big[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)\,\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal J}(G_*;0)\,(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)^\dagger
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)\,\widehat{\mathcal J}(G_*;0)^\dagger
+
\widehat{\mathcal K}(G_*;0)\,(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)^\dagger
\Big].
\label{eq:dSigmaJK_exact}
\end{align}

Decompose this into the shell-adapted frame
\begin{equation}
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
=
\hat n_\nu\,\mathcal S_\parallel^{(JK)}
+
e_{1\nu}\,\mathcal S_1^{(JK)}
+
e_{2\nu}\,\mathcal S_2^{(JK)},
\label{eq:SigmaJK_frame}
\end{equation}
where each \(\mathcal S_\bullet^{(JK)}\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix on the tangent doublet.

The odd witness projection is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O^{(JK)}
\propto
\frac12\Big[
\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal S_1^{(JK)})
-
\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal S_2^{(JK)})
\Big].
}
\label{eq:cO_JK_trace}
\end{equation}

Accordingly, the \(EE\)-row Hessian coefficient is the second \(\delta_E\)-variation of this odd trace:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
\propto
\partial_{\delta_E}^2
\Big[
\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal S_1^{(JK)})
-
\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal S_2^{(JK)})
\Big]_{\delta=0}.
}
\label{eq:H2EE_trace_reduction}
\end{equation}

This is already the exact projector-trace reduction of the first non-rigid odd test.

\section{3. Lowest-derivative local current ansatz}

The lowest-derivative local ansatz for the background-linearized Class II currents is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
m^a(P_0)\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r,
}
\label{eq:J_lb_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
(\partial_i\xi^a)\,
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
}
\label{eq:K_lb_final}
\end{equation}

Their Bloch-harmonic coefficients at the intervalley shell point are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
m^a(P_0)\,i(G_*)_i\,A_{G_*}\,
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\,(G_*)_j\,s_b,
}
\label{eq:J_harmonic_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\Xi_i^a(G_*)\,
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\,(G_*)_j\,s_b,
}
\label{eq:K_harmonic_final}
\end{equation}
where \(\Xi_i^a(G_*)\) is the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier coefficient of \(\partial_i\xi^a\).

Thus the shell-derivative matrices \(\mathcal S_1^{(JK)},\mathcal S_2^{(JK)}\) are explicit bilinears in the four background tensor inputs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0),
\qquad
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0),
\qquad
\Xi_i^a(G_*),
\qquad
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0).
}
\label{eq:four_background_inputs}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Final exact reduction of the \(EE\)-row}

Combining \eqref{eq:H2EE_trace_reduction} with
\eqref{eq:J_harmonic_final}--\eqref{eq:K_harmonic_final},
the first non-rigid odd test is reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\partial_{\delta_E}^2
\left\{
\frac12
\Big[
\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal S_1^{(JK)})
-
\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal S_2^{(JK)})
\Big]
\right\}_{\delta=0}
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:H2EE_final_reduction}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal S_1^{(JK)},\ \mathcal S_2^{(JK)}
\]
are built explicitly from the four background inputs in \eqref{eq:four_background_inputs}.

Therefore the \(EE\)-row is no longer a vague operator question.
It is a finite tensor-contraction computation on the frozen corrected branch.

\section{5. Folded-Bragg compression}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II bookkeeping, the derivative audit compresses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\,\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Talpha_foldedBragg}
\end{equation}

Hence the same \(EE\)-row may be read equivalently as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
\ \text{is controlled by}\ 
\partial_{\delta_E}^2\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),
\qquad
\partial_{\delta_E}^2\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:H2EE_foldedBragg}
\end{equation}
followed by the odd projector combination.

\section{Conclusion}

The first non-rigid odd microscopic test has now been reduced as far as is honestly possible without inserting the final frozen-branch background tensors.

The exact remaining data are only
\[
m^a(P_0),
\qquad
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0),
\qquad
\Xi_i^a(G_*),
\qquad
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0).
\]

Once these are inserted, \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\) is a direct finite projector-trace evaluation.

\section{First \(K\)-sector skew invariant for the odd channel}

The shell-relevant \(K\)-sector is determined by
\[
\Xi_i^a(G_*)
=
\xi_\parallel\,\hat n_i\delta^{a3}
+
\xi_E\,S^{(E)}{}_i{}^a
+
\xi_O\,S^{(O)}{}_i{}^a
+
\Xi_i^{a,\mathrm{irr}},
\]
\[
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
v_\parallel\,\hat n_j(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
v_E\,T^{(E)}{}_{jr}{}^{b}
+
v_O\,T^{(O)}{}_{jr}{}^{b}
+
\mathcal V_{jr}^{b,\mathrm{irr}},
\]
where
\[
S^{(E)}{}_i{}^a:=e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},
\qquad
S^{(O)}{}_i{}^a:=-e_{2i}\delta^{a1}+e_{1i}\delta^{a2},
\]
\[
T^{(E)}{}_{jr}{}^{b}:=(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b},
\qquad
T^{(O)}{}_{jr}{}^{b}:=(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}.
\]

In one convenient canonical orientation convention, the shell-relevant transverse coefficients induced by the \(K\)-sector obey
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
c_E^{(K)}\\[1mm]
c_O^{(K)}
\end{pmatrix}
\propto
\begin{pmatrix}
\xi_E & -\xi_O\\
\xi_O & \xi_E
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
v_E\\
v_O
\end{pmatrix},
\]
so that
\[
c_E^{(K)}\propto \xi_E v_E-\xi_O v_O,
\qquad
c_O^{(K)}\propto \xi_E v_O+\xi_O v_E,
\]
or, after an equivalent orientation redefinition,
\[
c_O^{(K)}\propto \xi_E v_O-\xi_O v_E.
\]

Therefore the invariant structural statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the odd channel is controlled by a transverse \(E/O\)-mismatch skew invariant}
}
\]
of the schematic form
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_K \sim \xi_E v_O-\xi_O v_E.
}
\]

Hence the first \(EE\)-row odd test is reduced to
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
\propto
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\,
\partial_{\delta_E}^2 \Delta_K\Big|_{\delta=0}
+\cdots ,
}
\]
up to a fixed convention-dependent normalization and possible subleading completion terms.

\section{Final Summary}

The \(K\)-sector has now been reduced to the canonical transverse pair
\[
(\xi_E,\xi_O),
\qquad
(v_E,v_O),
\]
through the exact decompositions of
\[
\Xi_i^a(G_*),
\qquad
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0).
\]

The structural content is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-parity pairings feed the even channel,}
\qquad
\text{cross-parity pairings feed the odd channel.}
}
\]

Therefore the first shell-relevant odd invariant carried by the \(K\)-sector is a skew transverse mismatch of the schematic form
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_K \sim \xi_E v_O-\xi_O v_E.
}
\]

Accordingly, the first non-rigid odd test is reduced to
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}
\propto
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\,
\partial_{\delta_E}^2\Delta_K\big|_{\delta=0}
+\cdots.
}
\]

So the next nonredundant microscopic task is no longer to inspect the full \(K\)-tensor,
but to evaluate only the four transverse scalar responses
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E,\ \xi_O,\ v_E,\ v_O
}
\]
on the frozen corrected branch.

\section{Exact Two-Source Split of the First Non-Rigid Odd \(E\)-Row}

\section{Goal}

We no longer treat the first odd \(E\)-sector test in terms of abstract scalar responses
\[
\partial_{\delta_E}\xi_E,\quad
\partial_{\delta_E}\xi_O,\quad
\partial_{\delta_E}v_E,\quad
\partial_{\delta_E}v_O.
\]
The uploaded notes already permit a sharper and more physical reduction.

The first non-rigid odd test is controlled by the exact \(E\)-sector current pair
\[
J_E,\qquad K_E,
\]
and \(K_E\) itself splits into two distinct microscopic sources.

\section{1. Exact \(E\)-sector current pair}

The exact completed \(E\)-sector pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_i M_E^a,
}
\label{eq:E_pair_J}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^a N_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:E_pair_K}
\end{equation}

Therefore the fast odd Hessian row is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:HEE_fast_exact_splitstart}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact two-source decomposition}

Substituting \eqref{eq:E_pair_K} into \eqref{eq:HEE_fast_exact_splitstart} yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\label{eq:HEE_two_source}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
:=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Bigg[
J_E
\left(
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
\right)^\dagger
+
\left(
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
\right)
J_E^\dagger
\Bigg],
}
\label{eq:HEE_proj}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
:=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
J_E\big((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\big)^\dagger
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\,J_E^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:HEE_qgrad}
\end{equation}

Thus the first non-rigid odd activation can come from exactly two places:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iF_E^a\neq 0
\quad\text{(projector/internal texture source),}
}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a\neq 0
\quad\text{(background charge-gradient source).}
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Rigid-truncation no-go revisited}

In the minimal rigid first-shell truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_iF_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_i\bar q^a=0.
}
\end{equation}

Hence both sources vanish simultaneously:
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}=0,
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}=0,
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}=0,
\qquad
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the rigid truncation fails for the odd channel for a completely explicit reason:
it kills both microscopic \(E\)-sector odd sources.

\section{4. Honest status of what is and is not fixed}

What is now fixed exactly is the two-source structure
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
\]

What is \emph{not} yet fixed separately from the current files is a fully explicit independent formula for each of
\[
\partial_{\delta_E}\xi_E,\quad
\partial_{\delta_E}\xi_O,\quad
\partial_{\delta_E}v_E,\quad
\partial_{\delta_E}v_O.
\]

So the correct microscopic decision problem is no longer phrased in terms of those four abstract scalar derivatives.
It is the sharper finite test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{which of }
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}},
\ H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
\text{ is the first nonzero odd source on the frozen corrected branch?}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The first non-rigid odd \(E\)-sector test is now fully reduced to two explicit microscopic sources:
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\quad\text{and}\quad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\]

Therefore the next nonredundant task is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{evaluate first whether }
\partial_iF_E^a\neq 0
\text{ or }
\partial_i\bar q^a\neq 0
\text{ on the intended branch.}
}
\end{equation}

Whichever of these survives first determines the first actual activation of the odd transverse coefficient.

\section{Why the first actual odd-source test should be the \(q\)-gradient route}

\section{Exact split already fixed}

The first non-rigid odd \(E\)-sector source is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the two literal finite tests are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O(\mathcal O_{E,\mathrm{proj}})\neq0\ ?,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O(\mathcal O_{E,\mathrm{qgrad}})\neq0\ ?.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Background availability of the \(q\)-gradient source}

For the locked one-defect background,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar q^a
=
\frac{\bar\Psi^\dagger T^a\bar\Psi}{\bar\rho}
=
z_B^\dagger T^a z_B
=:m_a(\theta),
}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,\partial_\theta m_a(\theta).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(q\)-gradient source is already present at the level of the locked one-defect background, provided
\[
\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\not\equiv 0.
\]

So the \(q\)-gradient route does not require any extra non-rigid internal completion beyond the background itself.

\section{Why the projector route is secondary}

By contrast, the projector/internal route requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iF_E^a\neq 0,
}
\end{equation}
namely a genuinely non-rigid internal/projector texture in the \(E\)-sector.

Thus the projector route is not the minimal first candidate.
It is a more refined completion channel.

\section{First-priority decision}

Therefore the correct first-priority odd audit is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute } \mathfrak P_O(\mathcal O_{E,\mathrm{qgrad}})
\text{ first.}
}
\end{equation}

Only if this vanishes or is symmetry-forbidden should one move next to
\[
\mathfrak P_O(\mathcal O_{E,\mathrm{proj}}).
\]

\section{Exact form of the first-priority object}

The \(q\)-gradient piece is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\big((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\big)^\dagger
+
\big((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\big)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\end{equation}

Substituting
\[
\partial_i\bar q^a=\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,\partial_\theta m_a(\theta),
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\big(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\,\chi_E\big)^\dagger
+
\big(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\,\chi_E\big)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\end{equation}

This is the first actual finite object that should now be evaluated.

\section{Honest status}

The statement is not that the \(q\)-gradient piece is already proven nonzero.
The honest statement is only:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{among the two exact odd-source candidates, the \(q\)-gradient route is the first one that is already background-available.}
}
\end{equation}

Hence it is the correct first computation target.

\section{Final Literal Overlap Test for the \(q\)-Gradient \(JK\)-Route}

\section{Status}

The \(q\)-gradient odd source is no longer structurally open.
It has already been reduced to one literal overlap decision.

The exact starting formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl(\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:qgrad_start_final}
\end{equation}

Since \(k_a(\theta)\) depends only on \(\theta\), and
\[
\partial_i\bar q^a=\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta),
\]
the only surviving derivative is the normal one.

\section{1. First decisive microscopic sign test}

The same expression reduces to the decisive sign test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\chi_E^\dagger
+
\chi_E(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:qgrad_sign_test}
\end{equation}

Thus the first unavoidable post-rigid odd source is controlled entirely by the overlap between the normal derivative of the \(E\)-sector current amplitude and the \(E\)-sector tangent fluctuation.

\section{2. Fourier reduction}

Expand
\[
M_E^a(\xi)=\sum_Q \widehat M_E^a(Q)e^{iQ\xi},
\qquad
\chi_E(\xi)=\sum_Q \widehat\chi_E(Q)e^{iQ\xi}.
\]
Then
\[
\partial_\xi M_E^a(\xi)=\sum_Q iQ_\xi\,\widehat M_E^a(Q)e^{iQ\xi}.
\]

Substituting into \eqref{eq:qgrad_start_final}, using the Hermitian symmetrization and the odd projector,
the \(q\)-gradient route reduces to the single shell-overlap decision
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right]
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:qgrad_single_overlap}
\end{equation}

This is the final literal overlap test for the \(JK\)-route.

\section{3. Honest status}

At this point the \(JK\)-route is not conceptually open any more.
It is data-blocked.

The literal evaluation of \eqref{eq:qgrad_single_overlap} still requires the actual frozen-branch harmonics,
schematically denoted in the notes by
\[
\bar A_G,\qquad B_G^{(E)}.
\]

Therefore the correct honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the \(JK\)-route odd audit has been reduced to one finite shell-overlap test,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{but its numerical sign decision still needs the frozen branch harmonic data.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

Inside the current frozen corrected branch, the first generic odd source is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
\]
and its entire microscopic decision problem is exactly the single overlap test
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right]
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\]

So the \(JK\)-route has been reduced as far as possible without inserting the frozen harmonics.

\section{Final Summary}

The \(JK\)-route odd audit is now fully compressed.

Its first generic odd source is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
\]
and its entire sign/nonzero problem is equivalent to the single shell-overlap test
\[
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right]\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

Thus the \(JK\)-route is no longer structurally open.
It is only data-blocked by the unavailable frozen harmonics.

If one wants an immediately forward-computable odd channel with the present data,
the explicit odd extra-carrier route is the correct next move.

\section{Adopting the Explicit Odd Extra-Carrier Route as the Active Forward Closure}

\section{Current stage}

The blocked \(JK\)-route is no longer the active forward path.
Its sharpest sign test is already known, but its literal shell-overlap evaluation still requires unavailable frozen harmonics.

Therefore the correct active forward closure route is the explicit odd extra-carrier branch.

\section{1. Minimal microscopic completion}

The minimal one-mediator truncation that explicitly opens the odd channel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trunc}}
=
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_E X_i^a \mathcal E_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:explicit_odd_trunc}
\end{equation}

The new ingredient that opens the odd extra-carrier route is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:odd_slot_active}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact explicit odd carrier}

On the embedded defect branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_O(\theta)=\Tr(S_OM_O)=\cos\theta.
}
\label{eq:qO_costheta_active}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit odd carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:IO_active}
\end{equation}

Its induced tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VEO_active}
\end{equation}

Hence the local transport densities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:local_density_EO}
\end{equation}

So the EO-slot is purely transverse and directly feeds the odd channel.

\section{3. Exact reduced coefficient dictionary}

Projecting to the Bloch zero modes gives the exact reduced sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:odd_route_dictionary}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:I3Ic_active}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the reduced first-order PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:odd_route_pde}
\end{equation}

\section{4. One-mediator coefficient point}

At one-mediator level, the coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_EJ_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\label{eq:tildeLambdaEO_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}

If one uses the transport-side canonical explicit normalization where the shell-basis factors are absorbed, then the lowest-order coefficient point is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:tildeLambdaEO_absorbed}
\end{equation}

Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,I_c,
\qquad
\beta^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_absorbed}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Exact nonzero conditions}

The odd channel is explicitly nonzero exactly when
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
I_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:odd_nonzero_exact}
\end{equation}

At one-mediator level, a sufficient concrete condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq 0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq 0,
\qquad
I_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:odd_nonzero_practical}
\end{equation}
and in the unabsorbed normalization also
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_OJ_1\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:odd_nonzero_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact project status after switching routes}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit odd carrier
\[
\mathcal I_O=X_i^{(O)}\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi;
\]
\item the exact EO-slot transport block
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\bigr];
\]
\item the reduced coefficient reading
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,\qquad
\alpha=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E,\qquad
\beta=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O;
\]
\item the one-mediator odd coefficient point
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}
\quad
\text{(in absorbed canonical normalization).}
\]
\end{enumerate}

What is still open:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic value/sign of }\widetilde\Lambda_O
\text{ beyond the lowest-order explicit one-mediator reading.}
}
\label{eq:still_open_tildeLambdaO}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The explicit odd extra-carrier route is now fully inserted into the reduced coefficient sheet.

The odd channel is no longer waiting on unavailable frozen harmonics.

Its exact branch-level formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,I_c,
\qquad
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
}
\end{equation}
and at the explicit one-mediator level this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_c
}
\end{equation}
in canonical absorbed normalization.

Therefore the active forward microscopic frontier is now reduced to the actual value/sign extraction of
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The blocked \(JK\)-route is no longer the active forward path.

The explicit odd extra-carrier route has now been fully inserted into the reduced coefficient sheet.

Its exact transport block is
\[
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\]
so the reduced coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\]

At explicit one-mediator level,
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}
\]
in canonical absorbed normalization, hence
\[
\beta^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c.
\]

So the odd channel is already explicitly forward-computable.
The only remaining microscopic problem is the actual value/sign extraction of \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\) beyond the lowest-order explicit reading.

\section{Exact Matching Between the Explicit Odd Route and the Canonical Mixed Odd-Active Target}

\section{Reference sheet}

The explicit odd extra-carrier route has the reduced coefficient sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:match_ref_sheet}
\end{equation}

\section{Target sheet}

The canonical mixed odd-active target branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
}
\end{equation}
with coefficient sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:match_target_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:match_target_trans}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact matching conditions}

Therefore the explicit odd route matches the canonical mixed odd-active target iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:match_long_exact}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,T_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\frac{\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,T_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:match_trans_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical mixed choice}

For the canonical mixed target
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\]
the natural matched explicit route is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0,
}
\label{eq:match_gamma_equal}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:match_gamma_perp}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:match_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
which reproduces exactly the canonical mixed odd-active transverse sheet.

\section{Equivalent coefficient reading}

Equivalently, in terms of the reduced transport-side coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2},
}
\end{equation}
so the target matching reads
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X T_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X T_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

For \(T_E=T_O=1\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E=\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\frac{\theta_0\kappa}{I_c}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

Hence the explicit odd extra-carrier route is not merely compatible with the canonical mixed odd-active target.
It can be matched onto it exactly by the finite relations
\eqref{eq:match_long_exact}--\eqref{eq:match_trans_exact}.

In particular, the symmetric choice
\[
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp
\]
is the unique minimal explicit route that reproduces
\[
\alpha=\beta
\]
at lowest order.

\section{Unified Reduced PDE Sheet: Reference Route Equals Canonical Mixed Target}

\section{Goal}

We now merge the current explicit odd extra-carrier reference route and the canonical mixed odd-active target into a single reduced PDE sheet.

The point is not merely compatibility.
The point is exact coefficient matching.

\section{1. Reference reduced sheet}

On the explicit odd extra-carrier route, the exact reduced coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c,
\qquad
\beta=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c.
}
\label{eq:unified_ref_sheet}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reference reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
+
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c\,
\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:unified_ref_pde}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Canonical mixed odd-active target sheet}

The canonical mixed odd-active target branch is fixed by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\Delta_{00}=\frac1{\sqrt2},
}
\end{equation}
with coefficient sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:unified_target_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:unified_target_trans}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact matching conditions}

The reference sheet reproduces the canonical mixed target iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:unified_match_long}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_E}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,T_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\frac{\gamma_O}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,T_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:unified_match_trans}
\end{equation}

For the canonical mixed target \(T_E=T_O=1\), the natural matched choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp\neq0,
}
\label{eq:unified_gamma_perp}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:unified_gamma_perp_match}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:unified_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
exactly as required.

\section{4. Unified reduced coefficient sheet}

Under \eqref{eq:unified_match_long} and \eqref{eq:unified_gamma_perp_match}, the current active reduced coefficient sheet is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:unified_final_sheet}
\end{equation}

So the active low-order reduced PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
+
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa\,
\Bigl(
(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2))
+
(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1))
\Bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:unified_final_pde_xy}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Rotated transverse form}

Define the rotated transverse coordinates
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_1=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2}.
}
\end{equation}
Then the same PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp^{\mathrm{mix}}
\bigl(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0,
}
\label{eq:unified_final_pde_rot}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{mix}}
=
-\sqrt2\,\alpha
=
-\sqrt2\,\beta
=
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:unified_vperp}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Interpretation}

So the current reference route is no longer merely a computational placeholder.

After the finite matching relations are imposed, it is literally the canonical mixed odd-active reduced PDE written in explicit one-mediator reference variables.

Therefore the practical active route and the structural target route are now the same sheet at reduced PDE level.

\section{Conclusion}

The exact unified active reduced PDE sheet is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
\]
and its rotated transverse speed is
\[
v_\perp^{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

So from now on, the reference low-order route and the canonical mixed odd-active target should be treated as one unified reduced PDE sheet.

\section{Final Summary}

The explicit odd extra-carrier reference route and the canonical mixed odd-active target are now merged into a single reduced PDE sheet.

The exact unified coefficient sheet is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Equivalently, in rotated transverse coordinates,
\[
v_\perp^{\mathrm{mix}}
=
\frac{\sqrt6\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Thus the practical active route and the structural target route are no longer separate at reduced PDE level.
They are the same matched sheet.

\section{Exact Active Reduced PDE from the Unified Matched Sheet}

\section{1. Unified coefficient sheet}

Take the already matched active reduced coefficient sheet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:active_sheet_final}
\end{equation}

Define for convenience
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\perp
:=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:aperp_def}
\end{equation}
Then \(\alpha=\beta=a_\perp\).

\section{2. Exact \(2\times2\) reduced symbol}

The reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{align}
A_1(p)
&=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\nonumber\\
&=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
a_\perp\Bigl[(p_1-p_2)\sigma_1+(p_1+p_2)\sigma_2\Bigr].
\label{eq:A1_active_xy}
\end{align}

Introduce rotated transverse momenta
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_1:=\frac{p_1-p_2}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_2:=\frac{p_1+p_2}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:q12_def_again}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\sqrt2\,a_\perp\,
\bigl(q_1\sigma_1+q_2\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:A1_rotated_symbol}
\end{equation}

Now define the transverse speed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp
:=
-\sqrt2\,a_\perp
=
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:vperp_exact}
\end{equation}
Hence the symbol may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
-
v_\perp\bigl(q_1\sigma_1+q_2\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:A1_Dirac_like}
\end{equation}

Therefore the active reduced PDE is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel \sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
+
v_\perp\bigl(
\sigma_1(-i\partial_{q_1})+\sigma_2(-i\partial_{q_2})
\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:active_reduced_pde}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact dispersion relation}

Because the Pauli matrices anticommute,
\[
\{\sigma_i,\sigma_j\}=2\delta_{ij},
\]
we have
\begin{align}
A_1(p)^2
&=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(q_1^2+q_2^2).
\label{eq:A1_square}
\end{align}

Since \(q_1^2+q_2^2=p_1^2+p_2^2\), the dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:dispersion_compact}
\end{equation}

Substituting the explicit coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{27\pi^2}{262144}\,
\alpha_X^2L_*^2\theta_0^6\kappa^6\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{128}\,
\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:dispersion_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact anisotropy ratio}

The active longitudinal/transverse anisotropy ratio is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_D
:=
\frac{|\lambda_\parallel|}{|v_\perp|}
=
\frac{3}{32\sqrt2}\,
\left|\frac{\alpha_XL_*}{\beta_X}\right|
\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\label{eq:anisotropy_ratio_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus the current lowest-order active reduced PDE is an anisotropic massless Dirac-type equation with exact finite anisotropy controlled by
\[
\frac{\alpha_XL_*}{\beta_X}\,\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]

\section{5. Exact \(4\times4\) Dirac embedding}

Now perform the opposite-valley doubling.
Let \(\tau_i\) act in valley space and \(\sigma_i\) in the tangent doublet.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^1:=\tau_1\otimes\sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2:=\tau_1\otimes\sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3:=\tau_3\otimes\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:Gamma123_active}
\end{equation}
These satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
}
\label{eq:Clifford_active}
\end{equation}

Therefore the doubled active Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(p)
=
-v_\perp q_1\Gamma^1
-v_\perp q_2\Gamma^2
+\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3.
}
\label{eq:HD_active}
\end{equation}

Squaring gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(p)^2
=
\Bigl(
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(q_1^2+q_2^2)
\Bigr)\mathbf 1_4,
}
\label{eq:HD_square}
\end{equation}
hence the same spectrum
\[
E(p)=\pm\sqrt{\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2(q_1^2+q_2^2)}.
\]

So the active unified reduced sheet is exactly a massless anisotropic Dirac carrier at lowest order.

\section{6. Nondegeneracy conditions}

The active reduced PDE is genuinely Dirac-type iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
v_\perp\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:nondeg_conditions}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:nondeg_conditions_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The active lowest-order reduced PDE is no longer merely a matched coefficient sheet.
It is an explicit anisotropic massless Dirac equation with:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
v_\perp
=
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\end{equation}
dispersion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2),
}
\end{equation}
and exact \(4\times4\) Clifford embedding
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(p)
=
-v_\perp q_1\Gamma^1
-v_\perp q_2\Gamma^2
+\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The active unified reduced sheet has now been turned into an explicit lowest-order PDE and Hamiltonian.

Its exact transverse speed is
\[
v_\perp
=
\frac{\sqrt6\,\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
\]
its exact longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
and its exact dispersion is
\[
E(p)^2
=
\lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1^2+p_2^2).
\]

Thus the current active lowest-order reduced PDE is an explicit anisotropic massless Dirac equation, not merely a symbolic target sheet.

\section{Explicit Sign/Value Audit of the Active Lowest-Order Reduced PDE}

\section{1. Overlap inputs}

The active reduced coefficient sheet is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_c\,\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_sheet}
\end{equation}

At the explicit lowest-order overlap level already evaluated in the notes,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_c=I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:signaudit_Ic}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_I3}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(I_c)=-\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\operatorname{sgn}(I_3)=-\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa),
}
\label{eq:signaudit_overlap_signs}
\end{equation}
for the convention used in the present notes.

\section{2. Longitudinal coefficient}

Using \eqref{eq:signaudit_I3},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_lambda_from_lambdac}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_c)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa),
}
\label{eq:signaudit_lambda_sign}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\lambda_\parallel|
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
|\lambda_c|\,|\theta_0\kappa|^3.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_lambda_abs}
\end{equation}

On the canonical witness branch, where
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_3,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:signaudit_lambda_Lstar}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\alpha_XL_*)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\label{eq:signaudit_lambda_Lstar_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Transverse coefficients on the explicit odd route}

On the explicit odd extra-carrier route,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}
}
\label{eq:signaudit_tildeLambdas}
\end{equation}
in absorbed canonical normalization.

Substituting \eqref{eq:signaudit_Ic},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{(1)}
=
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:signaudit_alpha_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{(1)}
=
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\alpha^{(1)})
=
\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X\gamma_E)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa),
}
\label{eq:signaudit_alpha_sign}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\beta^{(1)})
=
\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X\gamma_O)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\label{eq:signaudit_beta_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Canonical mixed target matching}

For the matched canonical mixed branch
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=\gamma_O=:\gamma_\perp,
\]
the exact matching condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}I_c
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_match_gamma}
\end{equation}

With \eqref{eq:signaudit_Ic}, this gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\gamma_\perp}{M_X^2}=-1.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_gamma_over_M2}
\end{equation}

Hence the matched lowest-order explicit route reproduces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_alpha_beta_matched}
\end{equation}

Thus the transverse speed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp=-\sqrt2\,\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt6\pi}{16}\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:signaudit_vperp_exact}
\end{equation}
satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(v_\perp)
=
\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa),
}
\label{eq:signaudit_vperp_sign}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|v_\perp|
=
\frac{\sqrt6\pi}{16}\,|\beta_X|\,|\theta_0\kappa|.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_vperp_abs}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Exact active dispersion with explicit absolute coefficients}

The active dispersion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
|\lambda_\parallel|^2 p_\parallel^2
+
|v_\perp|^2(p_1^2+p_2^2),
}
\label{eq:signaudit_disp_abs}
\end{equation}
that is,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
\frac{27\pi^2}{262144}\,
\alpha_X^2L_*^2\theta_0^6\kappa^6\,p_\parallel^2
+
\frac{3\pi^2}{128}\,
\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\label{eq:signaudit_disp_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Honest nonzero pass sheet}

The active lowest-order reduced PDE is genuinely anisotropic Dirac iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_XL_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_passsheet}
\end{equation}

If one wants the odd route explicitly active before target matching, one also needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O\neq 0
\qquad
\text{(equivalently } \widetilde\Lambda_O\neq 0\text{)}.
}
\label{eq:signaudit_oddpass}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

At the current active lowest-order sheet, the sign/value audit is no longer symbolic.

The exact overlap values already fix
\[
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
v_\perp
=
\frac{\sqrt6\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\]
and therefore the active reduced PDE is an explicit anisotropic massless Dirac equation with fully audited lowest-order coefficients.

\section{Final Summary}

The active lowest-order reduced PDE has now passed its explicit sign/value audit.

The already evaluated overlap integrals fix
\[
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

Hence the active longitudinal and transverse coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\alpha_XL_*\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
v_\perp
=
\frac{\sqrt6\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Their signs are
\[
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\alpha_XL_*)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\operatorname{sgn}(v_\perp)
=
\operatorname{sgn}(\beta_X)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
\]

So the current active reduced PDE is not merely matched and not merely symbolic:
it is an explicitly sign-audited lowest-order anisotropic massless Dirac equation.
