\section{Exact Longitudinal Sign Reduction to Background Matrix Entries}

\section{1. Closed finite formula}

In the current canonical branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\end{equation}

The reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,(u_{11}-u_{22})\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_entries_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact sign formula}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\alpha_X)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(m_\parallel)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(u_{11}-u_{22})\,
\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_sign_entries}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, since
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
\]
one may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel)
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\alpha_X)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(m_\parallel)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(u_\parallel)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Minimal canonical split}

Under the minimal explicit canonical split,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel=u_\parallel\Sigma_3,
}
\end{equation}
hence
\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}=u_\parallel,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=-u_\parallel.
\]
Then \eqref{eq:lambda_parallel_entries_final} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_minsplit}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact nonvanishing criterion}

The exact vanishing criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=0
\iff
\alpha_X=0
\ \text{or}\ 
m_\parallel=0
\ \text{or}\ 
u_{11}=u_{22}
\ \text{or}\ 
\theta_0\kappa=0.
}
\end{equation}

So once
\[
\alpha_X\neq0,\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
u_{11}\neq u_{22},\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
\]
the longitudinal slot is guaranteed to survive.

\section{Actual insertion on the explicit canonical witness branch}

Take the explicit witness branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0.
\]

The uploaded notes already give
\[
u_\parallel(T^1)=0.5,
\qquad
L_*(T^1)=0.5,
\]
and
\[
\lambda_\parallel=0.031883191949430,
\qquad
\alpha=0.340087380793916,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\]

At the same time, the exact branch formulas are
\[
u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac12\Re(\kappa_J),
\qquad
L_*(T^1)=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Re(\kappa_J).
\]

Therefore, in this explicit demo normalization,
\[
\boxed{
\Re(\kappa_J)=1,
\qquad
m_\parallel=1,
\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac12,
\qquad
L_*(T^1)=\frac12.
}
\]

Hence the longitudinal coefficient becomes
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X\,I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,\alpha_X\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

The active reduced symbol on this explicit witness branch is therefore
\[
\boxed{
A_1^{(T^1)}(p)
=
0.031883191949430\,p_\parallel\,\sigma_3
+
0.340087380793916\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\]

Equivalently, the dispersion is
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
(0.031883191949430)^2\,p_\parallel^2
+
(0.340087380793916)^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

Numerically,
\[
\boxed{
E(p)^2
=
0.001016537928884198\,p_\parallel^2
+
0.11565942657526601\,(p_1^2+p_2^2).
}
\]

The anisotropy ratio on this explicit witness normalization is
\[
\boxed{
\frac{v_\perp}{v_\parallel}
=
\frac{0.340087380793916}{0.031883191949430}
\approx 10.6666666666665.
}
\]

Thus the explicit canonical witness branch is already a concrete anisotropic massless Dirac carrier at the level of the finite audit demo.

\section{First-Order Corrected Insertion of the Longitudinal Scalar Package}

\section{1. Define the corrected scalar packages}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{JJ}^{\mathrm{corr}}
:=
\alpha_X\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}^{\mathrm{corr}}\,\mathcal N_{JJ}^{\mathrm{corr}},
\qquad
L_*^{\mathrm{corr}}
:=
m_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}u_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}.
}
\label{eq:GammaL_corr_defs}
\end{equation}

Then, in the same first-shell dominant normalization used on the explicit witness branch, the corrected longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\Gamma_{JJ}^{\mathrm{corr}}\,
L_*^{\mathrm{corr}}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3
+
O(\delta^2\theta_0^3\kappa^3).
}
\label{eq:lambda_corr_gammaL}
\end{equation}

\section{2. First-order expansion of \(\Gamma_{JJ}^{\mathrm{corr}}\)}

Write
\begin{equation}
A_{G_*}^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
A_0
+
0.0096\,A_A
-
0.0288\,A_E
+
0.0096\,A_O
+
O(\delta^2),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal N_{JJ}^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
N_0
+
0.0096\,N_A
-
0.0288\,N_E
+
0.0096\,N_O
+
O(\delta^2).
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{JJ}^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
\Gamma_0
+
0.0096\,\Gamma_A
-
0.0288\,\Gamma_E
+
0.0096\,\Gamma_O
+
O(\delta^2),
}
\label{eq:Gamma_corr_linear}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_0:=\alpha_X|G_*|A_0N_0,
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_X
:=
\alpha_X|G_*|
\bigl(
A_XN_0+A_0N_X
\bigr),
\qquad
X\in\{A,E,O\}.
}
\label{eq:GammaX_defs}
\end{equation}

\section{3. First-order expansion of \(L_*^{\mathrm{corr}}\)}

Likewise write
\begin{equation}
m_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
m_0
+
0.0096\,m_A
-
0.0288\,m_E
+
0.0096\,m_O
+
O(\delta^2),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
u_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
u_0
+
0.0096\,u_A
-
0.0288\,u_E
+
0.0096\,u_O
+
O(\delta^2).
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
L_0
+
0.0096\,L_A
-
0.0288\,L_E
+
0.0096\,L_O
+
O(\delta^2),
}
\label{eq:Lcorr_linear}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_0:=m_0u_0,
\qquad
L_X:=m_Xu_0+m_0u_X,
\qquad
X\in\{A,E,O\}.
}
\label{eq:LX_defs}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Fully reduced first-order formula for \(\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}\)}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Gamma_corr_linear} and \eqref{eq:Lcorr_linear} into \eqref{eq:lambda_corr_gammaL}, we obtain
\begin{align}
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}
&=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\Big[
\Gamma_0L_0
+
0.0096\,(\Gamma_A L_0+\Gamma_0L_A)
-
0.0288\,(\Gamma_E L_0+\Gamma_0L_E)
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
0.0096\,(\Gamma_O L_0+\Gamma_0L_O)
\Big]
+
O(\delta^2\theta_0^3\kappa^3).
\label{eq:lambda_corr_linear_final}
\end{align}

Define the three linear corrected response packages
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_A^{\mathrm{lin}}:=\Gamma_A L_0+\Gamma_0L_A,
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{lin}}:=\Gamma_E L_0+\Gamma_0L_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{lin}}:=\Gamma_O L_0+\Gamma_0L_O.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_lin_pkgs}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\Big[
\Gamma_0L_0
+
0.0096\,\Lambda_A^{\mathrm{lin}}
-
0.0288\,\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{lin}}
+
0.0096\,\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{lin}}
\Big]
+
O(\delta^2).
}
\label{eq:lambda_corr_compact}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Insert the explicit witness normalization}

On the explicit canonical witness demo,
\[
u_0=0.5,
\qquad
L_0=0.5,
\]
and therefore \(m_0=1\) in that normalization.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_A=0.5\,m_A+u_A,
\qquad
L_E=0.5\,m_E+u_E,
\qquad
L_O=0.5\,m_O+u_O.
}
\label{eq:LX_demo_norm}
\end{equation}

So the corrected longitudinal coefficient on the intended branch is reduced to the finite scalar input set
\[
A_0,\ A_A,\ A_E,\ A_O,\ 
N_0,\ N_A,\ N_E,\ N_O,\ 
m_A,\ m_E,\ m_O,\ 
u_A,\ u_E,\ u_O.
\]

\section{6. Practical sign-stability criterion}

A sufficient condition that the corrected branch keeps the same longitudinal sign as the base witness branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
0.0096\,\Lambda_A^{\mathrm{lin}}
-
0.0288\,\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{lin}}
+
0.0096\,\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{lin}}
\right|
<
|\Gamma_0L_0|.
}
\label{eq:sign_stability}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:sign_stability},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{corr}})
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\Gamma_0L_0)\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The longitudinal corrected branch is no longer blocked by missing structure.
It is reduced to the explicit first-order scalar package
\[
\Gamma_0,\ L_0,\ \Lambda_A^{\mathrm{lin}},\ \Lambda_E^{\mathrm{lin}},\ \Lambda_O^{\mathrm{lin}}.
\]

So the remaining task is literally the finite insertion of these corrected scalar responses.

\section{First Explicit Finite Package for the Corrected Transverse Coefficients}

\section{1. Fixed corrected seed}

Take
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}=(\delta_A,\delta_E,\delta_O)=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096).
}
\end{equation}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a\!\cdot\!\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}
=
0.0096\,a_A-0.0288\,a_E+0.0096\,a_O.
}
\label{eq:a_dot_delta_corr}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Base-plus-correction package for \texorpdfstring{$\alpha^{\mathrm{corr}}$}{alpha corr}}

Define the base even transverse scalar
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_0:=A_0X_1^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the linear response package
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_A^{\mathrm{lin}}:=a_A X_1^{(0)},
\qquad
\Xi_E^{\mathrm{lin}}:=a_E X_1^{(0)},
\qquad
\Xi_O^{\mathrm{lin}}:=a_O X_1^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the quadratic response package
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_A^{\mathrm{quad}}:=X_1^{(0)}Q_A(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}),
\qquad
\Xi_1^{\mathrm{quad}}:=A_0Q_1(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}).
}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\Big[
\Xi_0
+
0.0096\,\Xi_A^{\mathrm{lin}}
-
0.0288\,\Xi_E^{\mathrm{lin}}
+
0.0096\,\Xi_O^{\mathrm{lin}}
+
\Xi_A^{\mathrm{quad}}
+
\Xi_1^{\mathrm{quad}}
\Big]
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:alpha_corr_package}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, since
\[
\alpha^{(0)}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0X_1^{(0)},
\]
one may write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
\alpha^{(0)}
\left[
1+\frac{a\cdot\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}}{A_0}
+\frac{Q_A(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})}{A_0}
+\frac{Q_1(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})}{X_1^{(0)}}
\right]
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:alpha_corr_relative}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Pure-even branch package for \texorpdfstring{$\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}$}{beta corr}}

On the explicit canonical pure-even branch,
\[
X_2^{(0)}=0.
\]
Therefore the corrected odd transverse coefficient starts only at quadratic order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:beta_corr_package}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire odd transverse frontier is compressed to the single quadratic scalar
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}).
\]

\section{4. Exact quadratic Hessian form of \texorpdfstring{$Q_2$}{Q2}}

Let \(H^{(2)}\) denote the odd transverse Hessian matrix, with entries
\[
H^{(2)}_{AA},\ H^{(2)}_{EE},\ H^{(2)}_{OO},\ H^{(2)}_{AE},\ H^{(2)}_{AO},\ H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\]
Then
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
=
\frac12\,\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}^T H^{(2)}\delta_{\mathrm{corr}},
\]
that is,
\begin{align}
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
&=
4.608\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{OO}
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-2.7648\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EO}.
\label{eq:Q2_explicit_weights_again}
\end{align}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\Big[
4.608\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times 10^{-5}\,H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times 10^{-4}\,H^{(2)}_{EO}
\Big]
+
O(\delta^3).
}
\label{eq:beta_corr_full_package}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Practical dominance statement}

Hence the corrected even channel is governed by
\[
\Xi_0
\quad\text{plus linear and quadratic corrections,}
\]
while the corrected odd channel is governed entirely by
\[
A_0Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}).
\]

So on the present pure-even canonical branch:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{\mathrm{corr}}
\text{ is base-dominated and linearly correctable,}
}
\end{equation}
whereas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\text{ is purely quadratic and Hessian-controlled.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Conclusion}

The transverse corrected branch is now reduced to two finite packages:
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{corr}}
\leftrightarrow
(\Xi_0,\Xi_A^{\mathrm{lin}},\Xi_E^{\mathrm{lin}},\Xi_O^{\mathrm{lin}},\Xi_A^{\mathrm{quad}},\Xi_1^{\mathrm{quad}}),
\]

\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\leftrightarrow
A_0Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}).
\]

So the remaining work is not structural.
It is the finite insertion of

\]

\section{Exact optimization of the active longitudinal direction}

Starting from
\[
u_\parallel(T_\star)
=
\frac12\,\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr],
\]
write
\[
\kappa_J=|\kappa_J|e^{i\phi_J},
\qquad
\Delta_1:=c_1-c_4,
\qquad
\Delta_2:=c_2-c_5.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T_\star)
=
\frac{|\kappa_J|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_1\cos\phi_J-\Delta_2\sin\phi_J
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:upar_phase_split}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact canonical nonvanishing condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_1\cos\phi_J-\Delta_2\sin\phi_J\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:upar_nonzero_phase}
\end{equation}

Now impose the natural unit normalization on the active mediator direction in the active \(4\)-plane:
\[
c_1^2+c_2^2+c_4^2+c_5^2=1.
\]
Then
\[
\Delta_1^2+\Delta_2^2
=
(c_1-c_4)^2+(c_2-c_5)^2
\le 2,
\]
with equality iff
\[
(c_4,c_5)=-(c_1,c_2).
\]

Hence the maximal possible longitudinal splitting is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|u_\parallel|_{\max}
=
\frac{|\kappa_J|}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:upar_max}
\end{equation}

One maximizing choice is obtained by taking
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_1=\frac{\cos\phi_J}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
c_2=-\frac{\sin\phi_J}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
c_4=-\frac{\cos\phi_J}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
c_5=\frac{\sin\phi_J}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:Tstar_opt_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star^{\mathrm{opt}}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}
\Bigl(
\cos\phi_J\,T^1
-\sin\phi_J\,T^2
-\cos\phi_J\,T^4
+\sin\phi_J\,T^5
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Tstar_optimal}
\end{equation}

For this choice,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T_\star^{\mathrm{opt}})
=
\frac{|\kappa_J|}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:upar_optimal_value}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*^{\mathrm{opt}}
=
m_\parallel\,u_\parallel(T_\star^{\mathrm{opt}})
=
\frac{m_\parallel|\kappa_J|}{\sqrt2}.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_optimal}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we obtain the optimal active longitudinal coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{opt}}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512\sqrt2}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,|\kappa_J|\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_optimal}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact optimal-sign formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}(\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{opt}})
=
-\operatorname{sgn}(\alpha_X)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(m_\parallel)\,
\operatorname{sgn}(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\label{eq:lambda_optimal_sign}
\end{equation}
because \(|\kappa_J|>0\) carries no sign.

\section{Final Summary}

The longitudinal active-direction problem is now solved exactly.

Given
\[
u_\parallel(T_\star)
=
\frac12\,\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr],
\]
the optimal active direction in the normalized active \(4\)-plane is
\[
T_\star^{\mathrm{opt}}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}
\Bigl(
\cos\phi_J\,T^1
-\sin\phi_J\,T^2
-\cos\phi_J\,T^4
+\sin\phi_J\,T^5
\Bigr),
\qquad
\phi_J=\arg\kappa_J.
\]

It gives
\[
|u_\parallel|_{\max}=\frac{|\kappa_J|}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
L_*^{\mathrm{opt}}=\frac{m_\parallel|\kappa_J|}{\sqrt2},
\]
and therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{opt}}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512\sqrt2}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,|\kappa_J|\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

So the only remaining genuine longitudinal microscopic input is the actual sign/value of \(m_\parallel\).

must be checked using suborbit-resolved or explicit Bloch-resolved data.

It is blocked only by the final finite sign-resolved insertion layer.

\section{First actual transverse trigger on the sign-resolved suborbit basis}

\section{1. Fixed suborbit data}

The minimal sign-resolved first-shell basis is
\[
(A_+,A_-,E_+,E_-,O_{++},O_{+-},O_{-+},O_{--}),
\]
and the frozen corrected seed lifts to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{sub}}^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
(0.0096,0.0096,-0.0288,-0.0288,0.0096,0.0096,0.0096,0.0096)^T.
}
\end{equation}

The exact transverse rows are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r^{(ct_1)}_{\mathrm{sub}}
=
\left(
0,0,0,0,\frac14,\frac14,-\frac14,-\frac14
\right),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r^{(ct_2)}_{\mathrm{sub}}
=
\left(
0,0,0,0,\frac{1}{2\sqrt2},-\frac{1}{2\sqrt2},\frac{1}{2\sqrt2},-\frac{1}{2\sqrt2}
\right).
}
\end{equation}

Applying these to the corrected lifted seed gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r^{(ct_1)}_{\mathrm{sub}}\cdot\delta_{\mathrm{sub}}^{\mathrm{corr}}=0,
\qquad
r^{(ct_2)}_{\mathrm{sub}}\cdot\delta_{\mathrm{sub}}^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the current orbit-symmetric corrected seed still produces no linear first-shell transverse shift.

\section{2. First suborbit quartic completion is not yet transverse-generating}

The first explicit suborbit quartic completion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta M_{AE}
=
\xi\bigl(u_{AE}u_O^T+u_Ou_{AE}^T\bigr),
\qquad
\xi=-343.5328734898113,
}
\end{equation}
with
\[
u_{AE}=(1,1,-1,-1,0,0,0,0)^T,
\qquad
u_O=(0,0,0,0,1,1,1,1)^T.
\]

This is the first \(A/E\)-breaking but \(O\)-uniform quartic completion.

However, because the four \(O\)-suborbit loads remain equal, one still has
\[
r^{(ct_1)}_{\mathrm{sub}}\cdot Q_O^{\rm new}=0,
\qquad
r^{(ct_2)}_{\mathrm{sub}}\cdot Q_O^{\rm new}=0.
\]

Thus \(\Delta M_{AE}\) breaks coarse \(A/E\) symmetry, but does not yet generate a transverse witness.

\section{3. First genuinely transverse-sensitive directions}

The next irreducible sign-sensitive directions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_1=(0,0,0,0,1,1,-1,-1)^T,
\qquad
s_2=(0,0,0,0,1,-1,1,-1)^T.
}
\end{equation}

These are dual to the exact transverse rows
\[
r^{(ct_1)}_{\mathrm{sub}},
\qquad
r^{(ct_2)}_{\mathrm{sub}}.
\]

Hence the first genuinely transverse-sensitive quartic completions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta M_{t_1}
=
\kappa_1\bigl(u_{AE}s_1^T+s_1u_{AE}^T\bigr),
\qquad
\Delta M_{t_2}
=
\kappa_2\bigl(u_{AE}s_2^T+s_2u_{AE}^T\bigr).
}
\label{eq:first_transverse_patterns}
\end{equation}

These are exactly channel-selective:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta M_{t_1}\Rightarrow \text{nonzero }ct_1,\ \text{zero }ct_2,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta M_{t_2}\Rightarrow \text{nonzero }ct_2,\ \text{zero }ct_1.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. First executable transverse completion}

Therefore the first executable transverse-sensitive corrected suborbit kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\mathrm{sub}}^{\mathrm{corr}}
=
M_{\mathrm{sub}}^{(4c)}
+
\Delta M_{AE}
+
\Delta M_{t_1}
+
\Delta M_{t_2}.
}
\label{eq:Msub_corr_firstexec}
\end{equation}

At this stage, the transverse witness no longer depends on vague symbolic structure.
It depends on the two scalar trigger coefficients
\[
\kappa_1,\qquad \kappa_2.
\]

\section{5. Meaning for the reduced PDE}

The corrected transverse reduced coefficients are still read by
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{corr}}\propto (C_1^{\mathrm{corr}}\!\cdot\!G_*),
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\propto (C_2^{\mathrm{corr}}\!\cdot\!G_*).
\]

Therefore, at the sign-resolved suborbit level, the first actual transverse-trigger theorem is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa_1\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{the }ct_1\text{-channel can turn on,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa_2\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{the }ct_2\text{-channel can turn on.}
}
\end{equation}

So the real remaining transverse frontier is now reduced to the finite insertion of
\[
\kappa_1,\qquad \kappa_2.
\]

\section{Conclusion}

The first genuine transverse trigger has now been identified explicitly.

It is not the coarse \((A,E,O)\) correction, and not the \(A/E\)-breaking but \(O\)-uniform completion \(\Delta M_{AE}\).

It is the first sign-sensitive \(O\)-sheet completion
\[
\Delta M_{t_1},\qquad \Delta M_{t_2},
\]
with coefficients \(\kappa_1,\kappa_2\).

Therefore the actual microscopic PDE completion route has advanced to a strict finite transverse trigger audit:
\[
\boxed{
\text{determine the sign/value of }\kappa_1,\ \kappa_2.
}
\]

\section{First actual transverse trigger amplitudes}

Because
\[

\begin{equation}

\begin{equation}

because

\section{First corrected transverse coefficient insertion}

At first trigger level,

up to the already fixed branch normalization convention.

\section{Actual microscopic transverse coefficient extraction}

\section{1. Exact target objects}

The true microscopic transverse targets are not \(\kappa_1,\kappa_2\).
They are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
}
\label{eq:actual_Lambda_targets}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:actual_Mtddt}
\end{equation}

The projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr_{Q_B}(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
}
\label{eq:actual_projectors}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Dictionary to the reduced PDE}

Once \(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) are computed, the reduced coefficients are immediately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
}
\end{equation}

So the actual microscopic transverse frontier is exactly the evaluation of
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi),\qquad \mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi)
\]
on the frozen corrected branch.

\section{3. Exact executable chain}

The practical finite chain is already fixed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J,\ \delta K
\ \longrightarrow\
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD},\ \mathcal V^\mu_{DT}
\ \longrightarrow\
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
\ \longrightarrow\
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\ \longrightarrow\
(\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:actual_chain_transverse}
\end{equation}

At the leading mixed-channel level, the first active odd source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\cdots .
}
\label{eq:actual_H2odd}
\end{equation}

So the odd coefficient is not determined by shell-level trigger parameters alone.
It is determined by the actual one-defect Hessian projection.

\section{4. Honest relation to the shell-level trigger parameters}

The shell-level trigger coefficients \(\kappa_1,\kappa_2\) remain useful only as
sign-sensitive bookkeeping parameters for the first transverse activation patterns
\[
\Delta M_{t_1},\qquad \Delta M_{t_2}.
\]

They are \emph{not yet} identical to the actual microscopic quantities
\[
\Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

Thus the correct next computation is not to chase \(\kappa_1,\kappa_2\) further,
but to compute the source-differentiated kernels \(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD},\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\) explicitly.

\section{5. Final executable form of the current frontier}

The true remaining microscopic transverse problem is therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi),\ \mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi)
\text{ on the frozen corrected branch,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{project them to }
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT})\Pi_Q,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{then read }
\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O
\text{ by }
\mathfrak P_E,\mathfrak P_O.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Actual leading \(TD+DT\) differentiation and reduced transverse coefficients}

\section{1. Exact mixed-kernel form}

For the defect background
\[
P_B=z_Bz_B^\dagger,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\xi P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1 z_B^\dagger+z_B e_1^\dagger\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Hence every mixed shell--defect transport block carries one explicit factor of \(\theta'(\xi)\).

At the leading actual mixed-block level, the \(TD\) and \(DT\) kernels take the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
A_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
A_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right),
}
\label{eq:actual_VTD_leading}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
B_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
B_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right).
}
\label{eq:actual_VDT_leading}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q(V^\mu_{TD}+V^\mu_{DT})\Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
C_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
C_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right],
}
\label{eq:actual_MTDDT_leading}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E:=A_E+B_E,
\qquad
C_O:=A_O+B_O.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact projector readout}

Using
\[
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\]
the canonical invariant normalization gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12\,C_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12\,C_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

Thus at the minimal actual \(TD+DT\) level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:actual_Lambda_half_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Reduced transverse coefficients}

Since
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_E+B_E),
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_AB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:actual_beta_AB}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Honest remaining microscopic slot}

So the transverse frontier is no longer abstract.
The actual remaining microscopic insertion is exactly the finite one-defect differentiation that determines
\[
A_E,\quad A_O,\quad B_E,\quad B_O.
\]

Equivalently, the last transverse open slot is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(A_E+B_E,\ A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

Once these are inserted, the reduced transverse coefficients \((\alpha,\beta)\) are fixed immediately by \eqref{eq:actual_alpha_AB} and \eqref{eq:actual_beta_AB}.

\section{Actual one-mediator Branch-B coefficient formula}

Starting from the refined one-mediator truncation
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trunc}}
=
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^a X_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a
+
\gamma_E X_i^a \mathcal E_i^a
+
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a,
\]
integrating out \(X_i^a\) yields the shell-relevant mixed terms
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a,
\qquad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}K_i^a\mathcal E_i^a,
\qquad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}K_i^a\mathcal O_i^a.
\]

Let
\[
I_3
=
\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
J_1
=
\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\]
and let
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
denote the three shell-normalization overlaps from the projected \(2\times2\) shell matrix elements.

Then the actual shell-projected Branch-B coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3,
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_parallel_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E\,J_1,
}
\label{eq:actual_LambdaE_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O\,J_1.
}
\label{eq:actual_LambdaO_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2\bigr)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_A1_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical normalized form}

If one chooses the shell tangent basis so that
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,I_3,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,J_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_actual_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
-
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:canonical_actual_A1}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact nondegeneracy criterion}

The actual anisotropic Weyl symbol is nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\,C_\parallel\,I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X\,J_1\,(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:actual_mic_nondeg}
\end{equation}

So, assuming
\[
I_3\neq 0,\qquad J_1\neq 0,\qquad \beta_X\neq 0,
\]
the audit closes iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:actual_audit_closure}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact calibration audit table for the actual PDE completion route}

\section{1. Fixed reduced extraction layer}

The projected transport matrices are
\[
M_i
=
P_*
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}
P_*,
\qquad
M_\parallel=\hat n_iM_i,\quad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,\quad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
\]

Under the locked Pauli selection rule, the reduced coefficients are read by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\end{equation}

The exact Bloch calibration layer is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_\parallel g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Unit-channel calibration principle}

Let the transport-side coefficient point be
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O).
\]
Then the calibration constants are determined by the three unit-channel runs:
\[
(c\text{-unit}) : (g_c,g_E,g_O)=(1,0,0),
\]
\[
(E\text{-unit}) : (g_c,g_E,g_O)=(0,1,0),
\]
\[
(O\text{-unit}) : (g_c,g_E,g_O)=(0,0,1).
\]

If the locked Pauli selection rule is exact, then the calibration matrix is diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O).
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact audit table}

For the longitudinal unit run:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3 M_\parallel^{[c]}\bigr),
}
\end{equation}
where \(M_\parallel^{[c]}\) is the projected longitudinal matrix computed from the
\((c\text{-unit})\) microscopic run.

For the even transverse unit run:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1 M_1^{[E]}+\sigma_2 M_2^{[E]}\bigr),
}
\end{equation}
where \(M_1^{[E]},M_2^{[E]}\) come from the \((E\text{-unit})\) microscopic run.

For the odd transverse unit run:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2 M_1^{[O]}-\sigma_1 M_2^{[O]}\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. General mixed-case criterion}

If the calibration is not diagonal, one must instead use the full calibration matrix.
Then the exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Diagonal-case viability criterion}

In the diagonal locked case, the final microscopic viability test reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Honest remaining task}

Therefore the remaining microscopic calibration frontier is not conceptual.
It is the explicit evaluation of
\[
M_\parallel^{[c]},\qquad
(M_1^{[E]},M_2^{[E]}),\qquad
(M_1^{[O]},M_2^{[O]}),
\]
from the actual Bloch linearization, followed by the above Pauli traces.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact three-run calibration audit for the actual microscopic PDE completion}

\section{1. Fixed extraction layer}

The shell-projected transport matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_i
=
P_*
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}
P_*,
\qquad
M_\parallel=\hat n_iM_i,
\qquad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
}
\end{equation}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\end{equation}

The exact calibration layer is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_\parallel g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Microscopic source decomposition}

The longitudinal microscopic source is the \(OO\)-block primitive channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\end{equation}

The transverse microscopic source is the mixed \(TD+DT\) channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT})\Pi_Q,
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Definition of the three unit-channel runs}

We now define three microscopic calibration runs.

\subsection{(c-unit) longitudinal unit run}

Turn on only the primitive longitudinal source with normalized transport coefficient
\[
g_c=1,\qquad g_E=0,\qquad g_O=0.
\]
Equivalently, isolate the \(OO\)-primitive contribution and set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{unit}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Then the projected matrices satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{[c]}=C_\parallel\,\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1^{[c]}=0,
\qquad
M_2^{[c]}=0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal calibration constant is read by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[c]}).
}
\label{eq:Cpar_trace_audit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{(E-unit) even transverse unit run}

Turn on only the even mixed transport channel with normalized coefficient
\[
g_c=0,\qquad g_E=1,\qquad g_O=0.
\]
Equivalently, choose the invariant mixed block so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{\mu,[E]}_{TD+DT}
=
E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\end{equation}

Then the projected reduced matrices take the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{[E]}=0,
\qquad
M_1^{[E]}=C_E\,\sigma_1,
\qquad
M_2^{[E]}=C_E\,\sigma_2.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the even transverse calibration constant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[E]}+\sigma_2M_2^{[E]}).
}
\label{eq:CE_trace_audit}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\[
C_E=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[E]})
=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_2^{[E]}).
\]

\subsection{(O-unit) odd transverse unit run}

Turn on only the odd mixed transport channel with normalized coefficient
\[
g_c=0,\qquad g_E=0,\qquad g_O=1.
\]
Equivalently, choose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{\mu,[O]}_{TD+DT}
=
J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\end{equation}

Then the projected reduced matrices become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{[O]}=0,
\qquad
M_1^{[O]}=C_O\,\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2^{[O]}=-C_O\,\sigma_1.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the odd transverse calibration constant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[O]}-\sigma_1M_2^{[O]}).
}
\label{eq:CO_trace_audit}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\[
C_O=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[O]})
=-\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1M_2^{[O]}).
\]

\section{4. Off-channel leakage audit}

The locked Pauli selection rule is exact only if the off-channel traces vanish in each unit run.

For the longitudinal unit run, require
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[c]})=
\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[c]})=
\Tr(\sigma_1M_2^{[c]})=
\Tr(\sigma_2M_2^{[c]})=0.
}
\end{equation}

For the even unit run, require
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[E]})=0,
\qquad
\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[E]}-\sigma_1M_2^{[E]})=0.
}
\end{equation}

For the odd unit run, require
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[O]})=0,
\qquad
\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[O]}+\sigma_2M_2^{[O]})=0.
}
\end{equation}

If these vanish, the calibration matrix is diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O).
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. General non-diagonal fallback}

If off-channel leakage does not vanish exactly, define the full calibration matrix by
\begin{equation}
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda_\parallel\\
\alpha\\
\beta
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{\parallel c} & C_{\parallel E} & C_{\parallel O}\\
C_{Ec} & C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{Oc} & C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
g_c\\
g_E\\
g_O
\end{pmatrix}.
\end{equation}

Then the exact viability condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final executable audit list}

The next actual microscopic audit is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \(M_\parallel^{[c]}\) from the \(OO\)-primitive longitudinal unit source;
\item compute \(M_1^{[E]},M_2^{[E]}\) from the even \(TD+DT\) unit source;
\item compute \(M_1^{[O]},M_2^{[O]}\) from the odd \(TD+DT\) unit source;
\item read \(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O\) from the Pauli traces \eqref{eq:Cpar_trace_audit}, \eqref{eq:CE_trace_audit}, \eqref{eq:CO_trace_audit};
\item verify the off-channel leakage is zero (or record the full calibration matrix).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining microscopic PDE completion problem is now reduced to a three-run calibration audit.

The longitudinal normalization is extracted from
\[
C_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[c]}).
\]

The even transverse normalization is extracted from
\[
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[E]}+\sigma_2M_2^{[E]}).
\]

The odd transverse normalization is extracted from
\[
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[O]}-\sigma_1M_2^{[O]}).
\]

Thus the final open coefficient layer is no longer abstract:
it is the explicit evaluation of three projected trace quantities from the actual microscopic Bloch linearization.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit completion of the \(c\)-unit longitudinal calibration run}

\section{1. Primitive longitudinal seed}

The primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Its reduced transport-side output is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(\parallel)}]
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(\parallel)}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(\parallel)}]=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit overlap value on the seed profile}

For the explicit defect profile
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech(\kappa\xi),
\]
the longitudinal overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(\parallel)}]
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Unit-channel normalization}

Define the normalized \(c\)-unit input by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)
:=
\frac{2}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Then, by construction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel[\widehat V_{(c)}]=1,
\qquad
\alpha[\widehat V_{(c)}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[\widehat V_{(c)}]=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Projected matrix readout}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule, the \(c\)-unit projected matrices are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{[c]}=\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1^{[c]}=0,
\qquad
M_2^{[c]}=0.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the longitudinal calibration constant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[c]})
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3^2)
=
1.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Off-channel leakage audit}

The off-channel traces vanish identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[c]})=
\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[c]})=
\Tr(\sigma_1M_2^{[c]})=
\Tr(\sigma_2M_2^{[c]})=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the \(c\)-unit run is already exactly diagonal in the locked Pauli basis.

\section{Conclusion}

The first calibration run is fully closed on the explicit seed profile:
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel=1
}
\]
in the transport-side unit normalization convention.
Thus the remaining calibration frontier is reduced to the two transverse runs
\[
(E\text{-unit}),\qquad (O\text{-unit}),
\]
which determine \(C_E\) and \(C_O\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit completion of the \(E\)-unit transverse calibration run}

\section{1. Fixed transverse readout}

The reduced transverse coefficients are read by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\end{equation}

At the microscopic source level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit seed overlap}

On the explicit seed profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1}
u^2\sqrt{1-u^2}\,
\cos\!\bigl(\theta_0\sqrt{1-u^2}\bigr)\,du.
}
\end{equation}

Its small-\(\theta_0\) expansion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_c
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left(
1-\frac{\theta_0^2}{4}+O(\theta_0^4)
\right).
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Even primitive source and unit normalization}

Let the raw even primitive mixed source be the pure even channel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\end{equation}

Normalize it by the explicit overlap \(I_c\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)
:=
\frac{1}{I_c}\,V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi).
}
\end{equation}

Then, by construction, the corresponding transport-side coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(g_c,g_E,g_O)=(0,1,0).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced output satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha[\widehat V_{(E)}]=1,
\qquad
\beta[\widehat V_{(E)}]=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel[\widehat V_{(E)}]=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Projected matrix readout}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule, the \(E\)-unit projected matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{[E]}=0,
\qquad
M_1^{[E]}=\sigma_1,
\qquad
M_2^{[E]}=\sigma_2.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the even transverse calibration constant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[E]}+\sigma_2M_2^{[E]})
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1^2+\sigma_2^2)
=
1.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Off-channel leakage audit}

The off-channel traces vanish identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[E]})=0,
\qquad
\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[E]}-\sigma_1M_2^{[E]})=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the \(E\)-unit run is exactly diagonal in the calibration basis.

\section{Conclusion}

The explicit seed profile closes the second calibration run:
\[
\boxed{
C_E=1
}
\]
in the transport-side unit normalization convention.
Thus the only remaining calibration run is the odd transverse unit channel \((O\text{-unit})\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit completion of the \(O\)-unit transverse calibration run}

\section{1. Actual transverse dictionary}

For the actual microscopic \(TD+DT\) audit, the reduced coefficients satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta \Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta \Lambda_O.
}
\end{equation}

The invariant projector functionals are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Thus the odd microscopic source is read by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit seed overlap}

On the explicit seed profile,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Odd unit normalization}

Define the pure odd unit source by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal M}^{\mu,[O]}_{TD+DT}
:=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E[\widehat{\mathcal M}^{[O]}]=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_O[\widehat{\mathcal M}^{[O]}]=\frac{1}{I_\theta}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha[\widehat{\mathcal M}^{[O]}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[\widehat{\mathcal M}^{[O]}]=1,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel[\widehat{\mathcal M}^{[O]}]=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Projected matrix readout}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule, the \(O\)-unit projected matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel^{[O]}=0,
\qquad
M_1^{[O]}=\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2^{[O]}=-\sigma_1.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the odd transverse calibration constant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1^{[O]}-\sigma_1M_2^{[O]})
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2^2+\sigma_1^2)
=
1.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Off-channel leakage audit}

The off-channel traces vanish identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel^{[O]})=0,
\qquad
\Tr(\sigma_1M_1^{[O]}+\sigma_2M_2^{[O]})=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the \(O\)-unit run is also exactly diagonal in the locked Pauli calibration basis.

\section{Conclusion}

The third and final calibration run closes on the explicit seed profile:
\[
\boxed{
C_O=1.
}
\]

Hence the full calibration triple is
\[
\boxed{
(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O)=(1,1,1)
}
\]
in the transport-side unit normalization convention.

\section{Final Summary}

The three-run calibration audit is now closed.

Using the actual microscopic transverse dictionary
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
together with the explicit seed overlap
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
the odd unit run is normalized by
\[
\widehat{\mathcal M}^{\mu,[O]}_{TD+DT}
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
\]

This gives
\[
M_\parallel^{[O]}=0,
\qquad
M_1^{[O]}=\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2^{[O]}=-\sigma_1,
\]
and therefore
\[
C_O=1.
\]

Hence the complete calibration triple is
\[
\boxed{
(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O)=(1,1,1).
}
\]

So the remaining microscopic PDE completion problem is no longer calibration.
It is the explicit population of the coefficient point
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
\]
from the actual one-defect Hessian blocks.
